08:20:11","updatedTime":"2020-08-25 08:20:11","title":"How to Create the Perfect Email Marketing Strategy","link":"https://blog.aweber.com/?p=82477","description":"<p><img width=\"1200\" height=\"675\" src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/How-to-Create-the-Perfect-Email-Marketing-Strategy.png\" class=\"attachment-post-thumbnail size-post-thumbnail wp-post-image\" alt=\"Illustration representing creating the perfect email marketing strategy\" srcset=\"http://6elrmjmsbs335jwbeybarrry.wpengine.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/How-to-Create-the-Perfect-Email-Marketing-Strategy.png 1200w, http://6elrmjmsbs335jwbeybarrry.wpengine.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/How-to-Create-the-Perfect-Email-Marketing-Strategy-300x169.png 300w, http://6elrmjmsbs335jwbeybarrry.wpengine.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/How-to-Create-the-Perfect-Email-Marketing-Strategy-1024x576.png 1024w, http://6elrmjmsbs335jwbeybarrry.wpengine.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/How-to-Create-the-Perfect-Email-Marketing-Strategy-768x432.png 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1200px) 100vw, 1200px\" /></p>\n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Email is pretty darn powerful. In fact, for <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://neilpatel.com/blog/boost-email-roi/#:~:text=It's%20a%20whopping%204%2C000%25.,every%20%241%20spent%20on%20email.&amp;text=For%20example%2C%20your%20email%20ROI,you%20aren't%20tracking%20them.\" target=\"_blank\">every dollar spent on email, businesses earn 40 dollars return on their investment</a>.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>But before you can grow your email list, you need a plan. With an email marketing plan in place, you’ll have a better sense of what you need to do and who you need to target.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p><a href=\"https://martechseries.com/mts-insights/guest-authors/how-to-document-your-content-marketing-strategy/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">62 percent of businesses that document their content marketing strategy</a> consider it to be effective. In comparison, only 32 percent of businesses with an undocumented, verbal content marketing strategy believe it’s effective.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Plus, documenting your email strategy means you’ll be more likely to stick with it, reach the right people, and achieve your goals.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Creating the perfect email marketing plan that drives results doesn’t have to be difficult. Especially when you follow these 8 steps to a successful email marketing strategy.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>In this article we’ll cover how to:</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:group --> \n<div class=\"wp-block-group\">\n <div class=\"wp-block-group__inner-container\">\n  <!-- wp:group --> \n  <div class=\"wp-block-group\">\n   <div class=\"wp-block-group__inner-container\">\n    <!-- wp:list --> \n    <ul>\n     <li><a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/?p=82477#email-marketing-goals\">Choose Your Email Marketing Goals </a></li>\n     <li><a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/?p=82477#target-audience\">Define Your Target Audience(s)</a> </li>\n     <li><a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/?p=82477#right-esp\">Find the Right Email Service Provider </a></li>\n     <li><a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/?p=82477#build-list\">Build Your Email List the Right Way</a> </li>\n     <li><a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/?p=82477#tracking-doc\">Create a Tracking Document</a> </li>\n     <li><a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/?p=82477#calendar\">Create an Email Marketing Strategy Calendar</a> </li>\n     <li><a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/?p=82477#start-sending\">Ready to Start Sending Your Email Campaigns </a></li>\n     <li><a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/?p=82477#measure-performance\">Measure Performance</a></li>\n    </ul> \n    <!-- /wp:list -->\n   </div>\n  </div> \n  <!-- /wp:group -->\n </div>\n</div> \n<!-- /wp:group --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p><i>Prefer watching a video to reading? Check out the video version of this post.</i></p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:html --> \n<figure>\n <iframe src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/_I4PYddZtLA\" width=\"560\" height=\"315\" frameborder=\"0\" allowfullscreen=\"allowfullscreen\"></iframe>\n</figure> \n<!-- /wp:html --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"customTextColor\":\"#00539b\"} --> \n<h2 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#00539b\" id=\"email-marketing-goals\">1 - Choose Your Email Marketing Goals</h2> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>You wouldn’t run a marathon without training for the race. Similarly, you shouldn’t begin planning your email marketing strategy without setting goals.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Before you begin creating goals, take a moment to reflect upon what makes a good goal. Good goals are SMART goals. Here’s what SMART stands for:</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:list --> \n<ul>\n <li><strong>Specific</strong>: Avoid creating vague goals. Be sure to include details around how you plan to reach your goal(s).</li>\n <li><strong>Measurable</strong>: You should be able to measure your goals with specific numbers or checkpoints.</li>\n <li><strong>Attainable</strong>: When creating your goal, consider the resources you have. You need to make sure your goal is attainable with your current budget, time and skillset.</li>\n <li><strong>Realistic</strong>: Your goal should be challenging, but within reach. Review historical data or research industry benchmarks to determine what this means for you.</li>\n <li><strong>Time-bound</strong>: Give yourself a date by which you want to complete your goal.</li>\n</ul> \n<!-- /wp:list --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>When you create any goal for your email marketing strategy, make sure it aligns with these five guidelines.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:shortcode --> [bctt tweet=\"When you create any goal for your email marketing strategy, make sure it's a SMART goal.\"] \n<!-- /wp:shortcode --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Now, let's define your business's specific goals.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Not sure what kind of goals to set for your email marketing strategy? Consider your overall business goals for this year and improvements to your email strategy that could help you reach them. Write down a list of the areas where you’d like to improve and create goals from them.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>To get our creative wheels turning, you might want to focus on:</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3,\"customTextColor\":\"#af62ff\"} --> \n<h3 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#af62ff\"><strong>Growing your email list</strong>&nbsp;</h3> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>With a larger email list, you’ll be able to build relationships with more people, tell them about your business, and encourage them to purchase a product or service.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3,\"customTextColor\":\"#af62ff\"} --> \n<h3 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#af62ff\"><strong>Increasing your email open rates</strong>&nbsp;</h3> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>If a lot of people aren’t opening your emails, it’ll be impossible to keep them engaged and build a relationship with them. Addressing this problem could help you increase the number of subscribers you’re able to interact with.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3,\"customTextColor\":\"#af62ff\"} --> \n<h3 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#af62ff\"><strong>Improving your email click-through rates</strong></h3> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Good email click-through rates are a sign that people like your content and your business, which can impact their purchasing decisions.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3,\"customTextColor\":\"#af62ff\"} --> \n<h3 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#af62ff\"><strong>Decreasing unsubscribes and spam complaints</strong></h3> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Decreasing unsubscribes and complaints can help improve your deliverability and ensure you’re sending engaging, valuable content to your subscribers.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3,\"customTextColor\":\"#af62ff\"} --> \n<h3 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#af62ff\"><strong>Increase your email subscribers</strong></h3> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>When subscribers respond to your emails, you can communicate with them directly and build relationships that could encourage them to buy.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3,\"customTextColor\":\"#af62ff\"} --> \n<h3 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#af62ff\"><strong>Asking for — and implementing — subscriber feedback</strong></h3> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>By applying subscriber feedback, you can create emails that are more useful to your subscribers, which could help you increase open, click-through, and conversion rates.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>So how does this apply to you? Let’s imagine you set this goal for yourself:&nbsp;</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:quote {\"align\":\"center\"} --> \n<blockquote class=\"wp-block-quote has-text-align-center\">\n <p><em>I will grow my email list to 100 subscribers by the end of the year by adding a sign up form to my website and reaching out to my personal connections and asking them to join my list.</em></p>\n</blockquote> \n<!-- /wp:quote --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>This is a great example of a SMART goal. It’s specific because it describes exactly what you’d like to do and how you plan to do it. Since it explains the number of subscribers you’d like to attain (100), it’s also measurable.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>While a realistic goal will also vary from company to company, 100 subscribers in a year could be a very accessible goal for someone just getting started with email marketing.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>And finally, since this goal gives a specific date by which you plan to complete it, it’s time-bound.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Bottom line: make sure to create goals that are realistic and attainable for <em>you</em> with your current resources and limitations.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"customTextColor\":\"#00539b\"} --> \n<h2 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#00539b\" id=\"target-audience\">2 - Define Your Target Audience(s)</h2> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>After you’ve set goals for yourself, it’s time to determine who your ideal subscriber is and create a persona for this subscriber.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>By creating a persona for your ideal subscriber, you’ll be able to attract the right individuals to your email list and send content that’s relevant and helpful. This will guide your email marketing strategy moving forward, from how you grow your email list to how you communicate with your subscribers.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p><a href=\"https://twitter.com/NickWestergaard\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Nick Westergaard</a> of Brand Driven Digital says, “List growth is always key. But it’s not just about quantity. Quality matters. Who are you trying to reach? Who do you want to talk to more? How can you encourage them to sign up for your emails?”</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:shortcode --> [bctt tweet=\"List growth is always key. But it’s not just about quantity. Quality matters. -@NickWestergaard\" via=\"no\"] \n<!-- /wp:shortcode --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Your customer persona document should answer these questions:</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:list --> \n<ul>\n <li>What is your ideal subscriber like? Male or female? Age? Married or single? Kids? Occupation?</li>\n <li>What are their interests?</li>\n <li>What is their industry?</li>\n <li>What are their goals?</li>\n <li>What are their pain points and problems?</li>\n <li>What could prevent or stop them from buying your product/service?</li>\n <li>What type of content do they consume?</li>\n</ul> \n<!-- /wp:list --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>To answer these questions and get quality subscribers, you need to know your audience. Once you do, you’ll understand who you want to target and how you can encourage them to sign up for your list. And after they subscribe, you’ll be able to write emails that help them resolve their unique problems.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3,\"customTextColor\":\"#af62ff\"} --> \n<h3 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#af62ff\">Create your customer persona</h3> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Once you know who your ideal subscriber is, it’s time to create a customer persona that will guide your email marketing efforts. Your customer persona will take the information you gathered from defining your ideal audience and expand upon it.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>First, consider what your best customers have in common. You might even want to have a phone or email conversation with a few of these customers. Then, write down all the information you have about your persona in a document or on a piece of paper.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>For help creating your persona, I encourage you to use <a href=\"http://www.digitalmarketer.com/customer-avatar-worksheet/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Digital Marketer’s customer avatar (their name for a persona) worksheet</a>.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:image {\"id\":82478} --> \n<figure class=\"wp-block-image\">\n <img src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/Screen-Shot-2017-02-06-at-2.58.45-PM.png\" alt=\"Example of a customer persona avatar\" class=\"wp-image-82478\" />\n</figure> \n<!-- /wp:image --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"customTextColor\":\"#00539b\"} --> \n<h2 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#00539b\" id=\"right-esp\">3 - Find the Right Email Service Provider</h2> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Deciding which email marketing company to set up and send your email campaigns is a critical step. You need to make sure this company checks all the boxes you need to send beautifully designed emails.&nbsp;&nbsp;</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>If you’re already an AWeber customer, you already know about our incredible email marketing platform and award-winning customer service department, available 24/7, so feel free to move on to the next section - <a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/?p=82477#build-list\">Build Your Email List the Right Way</a>.&nbsp;</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>For those deciding between AWeber and another email service provider, here are just a few reasons why AWeber is the best choice for your email marketing strategy.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:image {\"align\":\"center\",\"id\":92699,\"sizeSlug\":\"large\"} --> \n<div class=\"wp-block-image\">\n <figure class=\"aligncenter size-large\">\n  <img src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/Graphic-of-AWeber-Features.png\" alt=\"Graphic of AWeber email marketing features\" class=\"wp-image-92699\" />\n </figure>\n</div> \n<!-- /wp:image --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3,\"customTextColor\":\"#af62ff\"} --> \n<h3 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#af62ff\">Create Easy &amp; Beautiful Emails</h3> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>You can create your emails using our <a href=\"https://www.aweber.com/email-templates-smart-designer.htm\">Smart Designer</a>, an AI-powered email template designer that automatically creates amazing-looking branded emails in just seconds. Or our easy <a href=\"https://www.aweber.com/drag-and-drop.htm\">drag and drop email editor </a>which allows you to create custom emails in minutes - no coding required.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3,\"customTextColor\":\"#af62ff\"} --> \n<h3 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#af62ff\">100s of Email Templates</h3> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Our mission is to do 90% of the work so you can spend more time building your business. That’s why we have a library of over <a href=\"https://www.aweber.com/html-email-templates.htm\">700 mobile-responsive email templates</a> for you to choose.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3,\"customTextColor\":\"#af62ff\"} --> \n<h3 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#af62ff\">Pre-built Email Reports</h3> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Easy to understand email reporting is important to any successful email marketing plan. That’s why we give you access to best-practice designed dashboards and reports. These reports are designed to deliver simple, meaningful insight into email and campaign performance.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3,\"customTextColor\":\"#af62ff\"} --> \n<h3 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#af62ff\">Email Automations</h3> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Assign triggers and flows to your emails that deliver the right message, to the right person, at the right time.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3,\"customTextColor\":\"#af62ff\"} --> \n<h3 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#af62ff\">Email Marketing Features</h3> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>What we talk about here only begins to cover the tip of the iceberg. AWeber’s <a href=\"https://www.aweber.com/email-marketing-features.htm\">email marketing features</a> include everything you need:</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:list --> \n<ul>\n <li>Industry leading email deliverability</li>\n <li>Automated tagging</li>\n <li>Personalized communications</li>\n <li>Email split testing</li>\n <li>Custom segmentation</li>\n <li>Landing page builder</li>\n <li>And so much more</li>\n</ul> \n<!-- /wp:list --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"customTextColor\":\"#00539b\"} --> \n<h2 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#00539b\" id=\"build-list\">4 - Build Your Email List the Right Way</h2> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>So far, you’ve laid out your email marketing goals, established your customer persona, and settled on an email service provider.&nbsp;</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Before you can send your emails, you need an email list. If you already have a list, I’m sure you’d like to see that list grow.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3,\"customTextColor\":\"#af62ff\"} --> \n<h3 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#af62ff\">How to Grow Your Email List</h3> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>The strategy you execute to grow your email marketing list may vary, but one thing must be consistent: your <a href=\"https://www.aweber.com/permission-email-marketing.htm\">customers need to opt-in to receive your emails</a>. Any email sent without permission is considered <a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/email-marketing/meet-the-anti-spam-laws-from-around-the-world.htm\">spam</a>.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Here are some <a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/email-marketing/how-to-get-email-addresses.htm\">permission-based email opt-in strategies</a>:</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:list --> \n<ul>\n <li>Put a sign up form on your Facebook, Twitter, or other social media pages.</li>\n <li>Have a signup form on your website.</li>\n <li>Experiment with pop up forms on your website.</li>\n <li>Create a lead generation landing page using <a href=\"https://www.aweber.com/landing-page-builder.htm\">AWeber’s Landing Page Builder</a>. Offer something of value in exchange for their email address.</li>\n <li>If you have a physical location, attend trade shows, or have a call center, simply ask for a potential customer's email address.</li>\n <li>Have a “Forward to a Friend” link in every email you send.</li>\n</ul> \n<!-- /wp:list --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"customTextColor\":\"#00539b\"} --> \n<h2 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#00539b\" id=\"tracking-doc\">5 - Create a Tracking and Reporting Document</h2> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>By tracking and measuring the performance of your email marketing campaigns you will be able to determine:</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:list --> \n<ul>\n <li>Your content performance</li>\n <li>Where you need to make improvements</li>\n <li>How frequently you should be sending emails</li>\n <li>Which lead source is performing the best</li>\n <li>The health of your email list</li>\n</ul> \n<!-- /wp:list --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3,\"customTextColor\":\"#af62ff\"} --> \n<h3 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#af62ff\">What Needs to be Included?</h3> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>An easy format to use is Microsoft Excel or Google Docs. Your document should include the following information:</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:list --> \n<ul>\n <li>Date of Send</li>\n <li>Audience (<a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/email-marketing/top-questions-email-list-segmentation.htm\">segments</a>) sent to</li>\n <li>A brief summary of the email</li>\n <li>Email Marketing KPI’s (Key Performance Indicators)\n  <ul>\n   <li>Number of emails sent</li>\n   <li>Number of emails delivered</li>\n   <li>Delivery Rate (Delivered/Sends)</li>\n   <li>Emails Opened</li>\n   <li>Open Rate (Emails Opened/Delivered)</li>\n   <li>Emails Clicked</li>\n   <li>Click Through to Open Rate (Emails Clicked/Opened)</li>\n   <li>Opt-outs</li>\n   <li>Opt-out Rate (Opt-outs/Delivered)</li>\n  </ul></li>\n <li>Post analysis comments</li>\n</ul> \n<!-- /wp:list --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3,\"customTextColor\":\"#af62ff\"} --> \n<h3 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#af62ff\">Why are Email Marketing KPI’s Important?</h3> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Each KPI tells a story about your email marketing strategy. Knowing how to read each statistic will help you determine what to test, leading to a more successful email marketing strategy.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Here we will focus on the main 4 email KPI’s:</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":4} --> \n<h4>Delivery Rate</h4> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Your delivery rate should be in the high 90s.&nbsp; Anything below this number needs to be addressed. A low delivery rate could be indicative of two things: poor list quality or the wrong email service provider.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Address your list quality first. If your sends are segmented by the source they signed up for your list (i.e. a form on your social channels or a landing page), see if one source is the reason for the low delivery rate. If the low delivery rate appears across multiple segments, consider <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://www.zerobounce.net/email-validation-api.html\" target=\"_blank\">cleansing your email list</a>.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:image {\"align\":\"center\",\"id\":92694,\"sizeSlug\":\"large\"} --> \n<div class=\"wp-block-image\">\n <figure class=\"aligncenter size-large\">\n  <img src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/graphic-delivery-rate.png\" alt=\"Delivery rate formula with example\" class=\"wp-image-92694\" />\n </figure>\n</div> \n<!-- /wp:image --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":4} --> \n<h4>Open Rate</h4> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Your email open rate is directly tied to your subject line and possibly your subheader. What is considered a <a href=\"https://help.aweber.com/hc/en-us/articles/204029726-What-is-a-good-open-rate-\">good open rate</a> will vary by industry, but on average, a healthy open rate may be anywhere between 15%-25%.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>If your open rate is low, consider testing different subject lines or preheaders to see what style works best with your customers.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:image {\"align\":\"center\",\"id\":92695,\"sizeSlug\":\"large\"} --> \n<div class=\"wp-block-image\">\n <figure class=\"aligncenter size-large\">\n  <img src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/graphic-open-rate.png\" alt=\"Open rate formula with example\" class=\"wp-image-92695\" />\n </figure>\n</div> \n<!-- /wp:image --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":4} --> \n<h4>Click Through-to-Open Rate</h4> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>There are several factors which could go into a low click through-to-open rate, such as your email design, your content, your call to action — really any element in the body of your email.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>It is a little more challenging to isolate what may be causing a low click through-to-open rate, which is why you need to set up some <a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/email-marketing/the-ultimate-guide-to-email-a-b-testing.htm\">A/B test splits</a> to determine the cause.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:image {\"align\":\"center\",\"id\":92696,\"sizeSlug\":\"large\"} --> \n<div class=\"wp-block-image\">\n <figure class=\"aligncenter size-large\">\n  <img src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/graphic-click-through-open-rate.png\" alt=\"Click through to open rate formula with example\" class=\"wp-image-92696\" />\n </figure>\n</div> \n<!-- /wp:image --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":4} --> \n<h4>Opt-out Rate</h4> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>We get it. It’s not fun to see people unsubscribe from your list. But, it happens to all of us.&nbsp;</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Generally a good (low) unsubscribe (or opt-out rate) is below 0.2%. But anything above 1% is a problem. Determining why customers are opting out can be a challenge, so be proactive. Set up a brief survey for people who do opt out asking why. </p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"align\":\"center\",\"level\":4,\"textColor\":\"very-dark-gray\"} --> \n<h4 class=\"has-very-dark-gray-color has-text-color has-text-align-center\">Example of an opt-out survey</h4> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:image {\"align\":\"center\",\"id\":92700,\"width\":525,\"height\":375,\"sizeSlug\":\"large\"} --> \n<div class=\"wp-block-image\">\n <figure class=\"aligncenter size-large is-resized\">\n  <img src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/opt-out-survey-example.png\" alt=\"Opt out survey example\" class=\"wp-image-92700\" width=\"525\" height=\"375\" />\n </figure>\n</div> \n<!-- /wp:image --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>This will help determine how to tackle the issue should it arise.&nbsp;</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:image {\"align\":\"center\",\"id\":92697,\"sizeSlug\":\"large\"} --> \n<div class=\"wp-block-image\">\n <figure class=\"aligncenter size-large\">\n  <img src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/graphic-opt-out-rate.png\" alt=\"opt out rate formula with example\" class=\"wp-image-92697\" />\n </figure>\n</div> \n<!-- /wp:image --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"customTextColor\":\"#00539b\"} --> \n<h2 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#00539b\" id=\"calendar\">6 - Create an Email Marketing Strategy Calendar</h2> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Creating an email marketing calendar will allow you to map out your strategy. The goal of an email send calendar is so you can easily view when you plan on sending emails and to which segments. It ensures that you send the right messages to the right audience at the right time. This will allow you to get the most out of your marketing efforts.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Create your calendar so it makes sense to you. Color code different segments or messages so you can quickly glance at your strategy.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:image {\"align\":\"center\",\"id\":92698,\"sizeSlug\":\"full\"} --> \n<div class=\"wp-block-image\">\n <figure class=\"aligncenter size-full\">\n  <img src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/02/email-marketing-calendar.png\" alt=\"Email marketing calendar sample\" class=\"wp-image-92698\" />\n </figure>\n</div> \n<!-- /wp:image --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"customTextColor\":\"#00539b\"} --> \n<h2 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#00539b\" id=\"start-sending\">7 - Start Sending Email Campaigns</h2> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Once you create your email marketing strategy, it’s time to set up and send your first campaign. Based on your calendar, you know the audience and message you plan on sending.&nbsp;</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>When <a href=\"https://www.aweber.com/create-email-marketing-campaign.htm\">creating your email</a>, you can start with an email template (AWeber has over 700 to choose) or you can use a drag and drop editor.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3,\"customTextColor\":\"#af62ff\"} --> \n<h3 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#af62ff\">Email Marketing Guidelines</h3> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Here are a few general email marketing guidelines you should follow when designing your email:</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:list {\"ordered\":true} --> \n<ol>\n <li>Add a logo to your email. Make sure people know who the email is from.</li>\n <li>Have a call to action based on the purpose of your emails\n  <ol>\n   <li>Drive traffic to a landing page</li>\n   <li>Trigger a phone call</li>\n   <li>Increase foot traffic</li>\n   <li>Place an online order</li>\n  </ol></li>\n <li>Make sure email laws are being followed for the country you are sending emails to. In the United States there is the <a href=\"https://help.aweber.com/hc/en-us/articles/204032256-What-is-the-CAN-SPAM-Act-\">CAN-SPAM Act</a>.</li>\n</ol> \n<!-- /wp:list --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"customTextColor\":\"#00539b\"} --> \n<h2 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#00539b\" id=\"measure-performance\">8 - Analyze Performance</h2> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>Once the email campaign has been sent, it’s time to analyze the results. Add the results of your campaign to the document you created to track your KPI’s. Figure out what worked, what didn’t, and how can you improve the email performance for your next send.&nbsp;</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>In order to optimize your emails, you may need to set up a series of A/B split tests for your next several campaigns.</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:heading {\"customTextColor\":\"#00539b\"} --> \n<h2 class=\"has-text-color\" style=\"color:#00539b\">Conclusion</h2> \n<!-- /wp:heading --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p>You don’t have to be a professional marketer to become an email marketing master. AWeber is here to help you. We have hundreds of tips to help you grow your business</p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:paragraph --> \n<p><em>Need more help getting started with email marketing? Get the full experience by checking out the </em><a href=\"https://www.aweber.com/email-marketing/?utm_source=awblog&amp;utm_medium=email&amp;utm_campaign=ultimateguide&amp;utm_content=article2\"><em>Ultimate Guide to Email Marketing</em></a><em>!</em></p> \n<!-- /wp:paragraph --> \n<!-- wp:image {\"align\":\"center\",\"id\":82371,\"linkDestination\":\"custom\"} --> \n<div class=\"wp-block-image\">\n <figure rel=\"noopener noreferrer\"><img src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/01/UG2EM-blogCTA-2.png\" alt=\"Ultimate Guide to Email Marketing\" class=\"wp-image-82371\" /></a>\n 1200w, http://6elrmjmsbs335jwbeybarrry.wpengine.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/03/MKT-9004-1200x675-Cover-300x169.png 300w, http://6elrmjmsbs335jwbeybarrry.wpengine.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/03/MKT-9004-1200x675-Cover-1024x576.png 1024w, http://6elrmjmsbs335jwbeybarrry.wpengine.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/03/MKT-9004-1200x675-Cover-768x432.png 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1200px) 100vw, 1200px\" /></p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Delivering the most relevant content to your audience is at the heart of any successful email marketing plan.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Sending targeted emails to groups or segments of your subscribers isn’t just a great way to deliver more relevant content to those who need it most, it also works. According to ClickZ, when using proper targeting, you can drive </span><a href=\"https://www.clickz.com/are-you-harnessing-the-power-of-the-email-channel/45340/\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">3x the revenue per email as compared to non-targeted emails</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Regardless of the number of subscribers you have on your email list, or your experience level with email marketing, email segmentation is something you can and should be doing.</span>\n<h2><strong>What is email segmentation and why is important?</strong></h2>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Segmentation happens everywhere. YouTube and Netflix suggest videos or shows based on your past viewing behavior. Amazon suggests products related to past purchases, searches, or products in your cart.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">It’s actually quite simple. Send people what they want and they are more likely to act.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The same is true with email segmentation. When you segment your email marketing, you’ll see:</span>\n<ul>\n \t<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Higher open rates</span></li>\n \t<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Higher click-through rates</span></li>\n \t<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Higher deliverability rates</span></li>\n \t<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Higher conversion rates</span></li>\n \t<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">More sales</span></li>\n</ul>\n<h2><b>16 ways to segment your email list and send targeted emails</b></h2>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Here are 16 ways you can easily use subscriber segmentation now or start preparing your list for when you’re ready to start sending segmented emails.</span>\n<h3><strong>1. Send different emails based on subscribers’ skill level.</strong></h3>\n<a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/email-marketing/email-courses-101-how-to-use-autoresponders-to-write-an-email-course.htm\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Educational email courses</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> are a perfect way to teach others and incentivize them to subscribe to your email list. To create this experience for people of varying skill levels, you can create beginner, intermediate, and expert versions of your course.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">When subscribers sign up and select their skill level, you can automatically tag them and send them the right course tailored to their needs.</span>\n\n<img class=\"aligncenter  wp-image-92183\" src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/segment-subscribers-skill-level.png\" alt=\"Segment subscribers based on skill level\" width=\"450\" height=\"485\" />\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">As subscribers complete the courses, you can create segments based on their skill level and send them emails to invite them to the next course based on their level of expertise.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In addition to a course, you can also use knowledge of your subscribers’ skill levels in other ways, like inviting them to a webinar or sending them videos and resources based on their needs.</span>\n<h3><strong>2. Send different emails based on your subscribers’ interests.</strong></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">If you send emails that cover a variety of topics, it may be helpful to learn what your subscribers are most interested in. Doing this will allow you to send targeted emails to segments who are more likely to engage with your content.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Gather this information when a subscriber signs up. Simply ask them what topics they’re interested in learning about, and tag them based on their selections. Then create segments of subscribers with those particular tags, or a combination of tags.</span>\n\n<img class=\"aligncenter  wp-image-92185\" src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/03/segment-subscribers-interests.png\" alt=\"Segment subscribers based on interests\" width=\"450\" height=\"585\" />\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">You can also gather this information when subscribers click on links in your emails. If you send out an email about a new vegan recipe, you can tag subscribers with the word “vegan” when they click the link for the recipe.</span>\n<h3><strong>3. Send emails with a gift based on subscribers’ birth month.</strong></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Most people love receiving birthday wishes. Send your subscribers a birthday gift or incentive during their birth month.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">On your sign up form, ask subscribers to choose their birth month and set up custom fields to apply a tag based on their selection. Each month, send an email with a birthday gift to the corresponding group of tagged subscribers.</span>\n<h3><strong>4. Send emails in subscribers’ native language.</strong></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">If you have subscribers from different countries around the world, you might assume that their native language is different from your own. As a result, you can segment these subscribers and send emails in their preferred language.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Whether you </span><a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/email-marketing/5-minute-email-tips-sending-segmented-emails.htm\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">segment and tag subscribers based on their geographic location</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> or ask them for their language preference in the sign up form, you can easily deliver content that’s accessible to everyone.</span>\n<h3><strong>5. Send emails based on subscribers’ geographic locations.</strong></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Run events in different locations? Have an ecommerce shop with a global customer base? </span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">By segmenting subscribers based on their geographic location, you can send contextual emails with content, like upcoming events near them and exclusive discounts for local holidays or seasons. Or share advice and news that would be more relevant to that particular audience.</span>\n\n<img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-92186\" src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/03/segment-customers-location.png\" alt=\"Segment subscribers based on location\" width=\"1770\" height=\"268\" />\n<h3><strong>6. Send contextual welcome campaigns based on different incentives, sign up forms, or landing pages.</strong></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Do you offer multiple incentives on different sign up forms or landing pages? Make sure your subscribers get </span><a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/email-marketing/welcome-email-campaigns-101-how-to-create-an-awesome-welcome-campaign.htm\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">welcome emails</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> that relate to the incentive for which they signed up. </span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Apply unique tags to subscribers who sign up to deliver the right incentive to the right person, and create a more personalized email campaign.</span>\n\n<img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-92187\" src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/03/segment-customers-automated-campaigns-multiple-incentives.png\" alt=\"Segment subscribers based on different opt-in incentives\" width=\"2782\" height=\"1092\" />\n<h3><strong>7. Send an email based on the incentive for which a subscriber signed up.</strong></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In addition to sending contextual welcome campaigns to subscribers based on what they signed up for, you can also send targeted broadcasts with content that relates to the incentive. Since you already know they’re interested in a specific topic, you can continue sending them targeted content they’ll enjoy.</span>\n\n<img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-92188\" src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/03/segment-sign-up-forms-multiple-incentives.png\" alt=\"Segment subscribers based on the incentive they signed up for\" width=\"2822\" height=\"1370\" />\n<h3><strong>8. Send win-back (or re-engagement) emails to inactive subscribers.</strong></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">People sign up to your email list for all sorts of reasons, so it’s normal that some become inactive over time. But when you continue to send emails to unengaged subscribers, you’re only hurting your email performance and deliverability.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">If you have subscribers who haven’t engaged with your emails in a long time, try to win them back and </span><a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/email-marketing/re-engagement-emails-content.htm\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">get them engaged with a targeted broadcast or automated campaign</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.</span>\n\n<img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-92189\" src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/03/segment-inactive-subscribers.png\" alt=\"How to create a segment of inactive subscribers\" width=\"1772\" height=\"462\" />\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">In your email, explain what they’re missing out on and offer exclusive discounts and incentives to get them to take action. If they click the incentive, keep them on your email list. And if they don’t, simply unsubscribe or remove them. A smaller, more engaged list is generally better than a larger, unengaged list.</span>\n<h3><strong>9. Send a second email or trigger a campaign to subscribers who opened the first email, but didn’t click a link.</strong></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Notice a low click-through rate in your previous email? Create a segment of subscribers who opened your message, but didn’t click. Then send them a second email to encourage them to click through.</span>\n\n<img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-92190\" src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/03/segment-subscribers-opened-email-not-clicked.png\" alt=\"How to create a segment of subscribers who opened a message but didn't click the link\" width=\"1770\" height=\"364\" />\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Consider how you might be able to make the message more appealing for this segment of subscribers. This could mean emphasizing the value proposition of the action you want them to take, adding more urgency to your content or even trying new call-to-action copy.</span>\n<h3><strong>10. Send a second email or trigger a campaign to subscribers who clicked a link in an email.</strong></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">To send emails to subscribers based on actions they </span><i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">did</span></i><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> take, create a subscriber segment based on a link they clicked in a previous email. You can send a targeted email to those tagged subscribers for specific products they might be interested in, or you can enter them into a new automated campaign.</span>\n<h3><strong>11. Send emails based on pages subscribers have visited — or not visited — on your website.</strong></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Want to tailor your emails based on the pages your subscribers visit on your website? Use </span><a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/new-features/monetizing-your-web-traffic.htm\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">AWeber’s event tracking feature</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> to track subscribers’ activity on your website and automatically tag them based on the pages they have visited.</span>\n\n<img class=\"aligncenter  wp-image-92191\" src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/03/segment-subscribers-website-traffic.png\" alt=\"Create a segment of subscribers based on the web pages they've visited\" width=\"450\" height=\"569\" />\n\n<b>Pro tip:</b><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> If you’re using AWeber’s landing pages, event tracking is built in.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Create segments of subscribers who have visited or not visited specific pages on your site, and send tailored broadcasts or triggers campaigns to those subscribers.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Want to learn why subscribers aren’t making it through the sales funnel? Create a segment of subscribers who visit the first page of your funnel, but not the next one. Send them a broadcast or trigger an automated campaign to invite feedback to learn what stopped them from progressing.</span>\n<h3><strong>12. Send emails to new subscribers or customers.</strong></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Automated welcome emails are great for engaging your new subscribers. But you can also create segments of new subscribers and send targeted broadcasts to invite them to new-customer events, webinars, and more.</span>\n\n<img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-92192\" src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/03/segment-new-subscribers.png\" alt=\"How to create a segment of new subscribers\" width=\"1770\" height=\"364\" />\n<h3><strong>13. Send emails to long-time subscribers or customers.</strong></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">According to Motista, customers who form an emotional connection with your business have over </span><a href=\"https://www.motista.com/resource/leveraging-value-emotional-connection-retailers\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">300% higher lifetime value</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> than those who don’t.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Reward your most loyal subscribers. Create a segment of long-time subscribers and thank them for their loyalty. Offer them VIP perks, invite them to special loyalty events, get to know them, and gather feedback from them.</span>\n\n<img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-92193\" src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2017/03/segment-long-time-customers.png\" alt=\"How to create a segment of long-time subscribers\" width=\"1770\" height=\"366\" />\n<h3><strong>14. Send emails based on survey results.</strong></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Gathering feedback is critical to any business, entrepreneur, or creator. Survey your audience regularly, and create segments of subscribers who rated you or your products favorably, as well as unfavorably. Follow up with them by sending an email to thank them for their feedback and to gain more insight from their input.</span>\n<h3><strong>15. Send different emails to customers and potential buyers.</strong></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">By </span><a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/email-marketing/creating-personalized-email-campaigns-for-a-course.htm\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">segmenting subscribers based on whether or not they’re a current customer</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, you can target your promotional messages to include more relevant content.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Use customer segmentation to separate your customers and potential clients into separate groups you can speak to differently.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Instead of sending an email to existing customers and asking them to purchase your product or service, you can speak more to their loyalty and promote advocacy and ongoing interaction.</span>\n<h3><strong>16. Send emails about products based on potential buyers’ gender.</strong></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Personalizing the product suggestions for each subscriber can help convert them into customers. </span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">For instance, if you’re a retailer that sells clothing products by gender, simply tag subscribers based on their preferences and create segments of customers who are interested in each of these types of products. Then personalize your emails with relevant products based on their gender choice.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Use </span><a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/email-marketing/aweber-dynamic-email-content-feature.htm\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">dynamic email content</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> to display the most relevant products for your potential buyer.</span>\n<h2><b>4 bonus ecommerce segmentation strategies</b></h2>\n<h3><strong>1. Send emails based on products customers purchase.</strong></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">By segmenting your customers based on the products they purchased, you’re able to tailor your emails to invite feedback or reviews on those products. You can also send promotional emails to upsell them on upgrades, cross-sell related products or services, and encourage repeat sales.</span>\n<h3><strong>2. Send emails based on products potential buyers left in their shopping cart.</strong></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Create a segment of subscribers who left something in their shopping cart. You can send an automated cart abandonment campaign to let them know they left something in their cart and encourage them to come back to complete their purchase. </span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Consider offering them a discount or other incentive to entice them to click through and complete their purchase.</span>\n<h3><strong>3. Send emails based on products potential buyers expressed interest in, but didn’t buy.</strong></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Perhaps someone clicked a link in your email to check out your product or service, but didn’t make the purchase. Create a segment of these subscribers and send them an email asking for feedback on their experience. Was there something about the product or service they didn’t like?</span>\n<h3><strong>4. Send emails to subscribers with a minimum purchase amount or purchase price range.</strong></h3>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Want to connect with your high-value customers? Create a segment of customers who have purchased your highest-value products. Perhaps send them a thank you email, or offer them VIP perks.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Use </span><a href=\"https://help.aweber.com/hc/en-us/articles/204029696-How-do-I-set-up-Sales-Tracking-\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">AWeber’s sales tracking feature</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> to track who makes a purchase after clicking a link to your product or service in your email. Then create a segment of customers who purchased a product with a minimum purchase price or within a price range.</span>\n<h2><strong>Start tagging subscribers today.</strong></h2>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Not sure if you want to send targeted emails right now? You can always start tagging subscribers now in case you want to do so later.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Add tags to your sign up form or landing page to ensure every subscriber gets it when they sign up. If you have multiple sign up forms or landing pages on one list, for example, this will allow you to know exactly where your subscribers came from.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Plus, if you decide you want to send subscribers that signed up for your checklist an invite to a webinar on the same topic, you can do so with ease.</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Haven’t been tagging subscribers and want to go back and tag them anyway? Search for subscribers using the </span><a href=\"https://help.aweber.com/hc/en-us/articles/204027486-How-do-I-use-ad-tracking-with-my-sign-up-form-\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">ad tracking code</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> associated with your AWeber sign up form, or the “</span><a href=\"https://help.aweber.com/hc/en-us/articles/204029036-What-is-an-Add-URL-\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Add URL</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">” for your landing page, and </span><a href=\"https://help.aweber.com/hc/en-us/articles/360008220453-How-do-I-add-or-remove-tags-in-bulk-\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">bulk apply a tag</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">.</span>\n<h2><strong>Segment subscribers. Send more relevant emails.</strong></h2>\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Sending targeted emails to subscriber segments is a proven way to improve your email engagement and ROI. So what are you waiting for?</span>\n\n<span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">This post only listed some of the many ways in which you can segment your list, but if you have other plans to segment subscribers, we’d love to hear about them in the comments below!</span><p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/email-marketing/16-ways-to-segment-subscribers.htm\">16 Ways Email /03/segment-long-time-customers.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn76@2020_3/2020/08/25/00-20-15-664_96c76d1571149b73.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1598314811731},{"createdTime":"2020-08-25 -->\n<p>You have an awesome&#160; product or service. And you know it adds value to your target audience. All of the marketing research and testing has told you that.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Now all you need to do is convince people to choose you over your competition. But how?&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>A high performing landing page —also referred to as a Lead Page— will help you not only attract new visitors, but collect their information so you can. send them emails to tell them about the value of your offer.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Whether you’re looking to drive sales, sign ups, or downloads, a highly optimized landing page can provide real value by bringing your visitors to a page targeted directly to their needs.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>According to a report by truelist.com, a landing page tailored to the needs of your customer can <a href=\"https://truelist.co/blog/landing-page-statistics/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">increase conversion by 300%</a>.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>But how do you know what landing page best practices to achieve your desired action?&#160; We’re here to help with these 10 steps to create landing pages that convert.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph {\"align\":\"center\"} -->\n<p class=\"has-text-align-center\"><em>(You can create a landing page in minutes with AWeber's Landing Page Builder)&#160;</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:buttons {\"align\":\"center\"} -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-buttons aligncenter\"><!-- wp:button {\"textColor\":\"very-dark-gray\",\"customBackgroundColor\":\"#ffaf62\",\"borderRadius\":0} -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-button\"><a class=\"wp-block-button__link has-text-color has-very-dark-gray-color has-background no-border-radius\" href=\"https://www.aweber.com/free.htm?utm_source=awblog&#38;utm_medium=email&#38;utm_campaign=blogcontent&#38;utm_content=blogpost88746-landingpagetrial\" style=\"background-color:#ffaf62\">Get started with AWeber Free</a></div>\n<!-- /wp:button --></div>\n<!-- /wp:buttons -->\n\n<h2>Keep the Design Clean and Simple</h2>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Many landing pages suffer because there’s just too much going on. Approach landing page design with a feeling of respect for the time of the visitor. By making a clear and digestible landing page, you can do more with content because you aren’t forced to slam a loud call-to-action button awkwardly into a crowded space.&#160;</span></p>\n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Focus on the Primary Goals of the Campaign</span></h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Remember, everything about your landing page should be geared towards getting the user to convert. This means removing anything that might draw their attention away from your offer.&#160;&#160;</span></p>\n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Use of White Space</span></h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">White space is an important part of email landing page design, so make the most of it. Sometimes, what you leave off the page is as powerful as what you include. White space removes congestion and gives the brain space to think. It also forces the eyes to focus on your offer.</span></p>\n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Optimize your Landing Page Space</span></h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Make your landing page full width and height, and remove navigation features. This isn’t to say you should scrap scrolling completely, but you should take away any visible arrows or buttons that encourage it.</span></p>\n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Simple Design Landing Page Example</span></h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Take a look at how the </span><a href=\"https://www.aweber.com/?utm_source=awblog&#38;utm_medium=email&#38;utm_campaign=blogcontent&#38;utm_content=blogcontent021219webcomhomepage\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">AWeber</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> landing page keeps things simple and clean.&#160; Your focus goes to the benefit headline and then follows a natural path to the call to action button:</span></p>\n<p><a href=\"http://www.aweber.com/\"><img class=\"aligncenter wp-image-91773 size-large\" src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/02/unnamed-4-1024x618.png\" alt=\"AWeber simple landing page example\" width=\"640\" height=\"386\"/></a></p>\n<h2><strong>Create landing page headlines that hit home</strong></h2>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">The headline on the landing page is the first thing that visitors see, so it needs to capture their attention immediately and convey your unique value proposition (more on this below). If it’s vague or doesn’t convey a benefit, users won’t stick around long enough to convert.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">A landing page will live or die on the strength of its headline. This is what grabs a visitor’s attention and compels them to find out more about your offer.</span></p>\n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Landing Page Case Study</span></h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">As many as </span><a href=\"https://moz.com/blog/5-data-insights-into-the-headlines-readers-click\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noreferrer noopener\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">80% of people will read the average headline, but only 20% will read the rest of the copy</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, so it’s important that you nail this part of your page.</span></p>\n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Elements of Headline</span></h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">A good catchy headline should:</span></p>\n<ul>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Immediately grab the attention of your visitors</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Tell the visitor what your offer is about</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Be short and sweet</span></li>\n</ul>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Once the headline has the user invested, you can reinforce your message with a powerful subheadline that persuades them to stay. Your subheadline can go into more detail than the main headline, but you should limit it to no more than a few lines of persuasive copy.</span></p>\n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Landing Page Examples Focusing on Headlines</span></h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">This example from </span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Robinhood</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> is as simple yet powerful, due to the strong headline.</span></p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-88752 size-full\" src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/02/Article-Image-4.jpg\" alt=\"landing page example focusing on headlines\" width=\"740\" height=\"499\"/></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Get proven, eye-catching landing page headline formulas in our guide, </span><a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/landing-page-guide\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">How to Write Landing Pages That Convert. </span></a></p>\n<h2><strong>Grab attention with landing page images</strong></h2>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Humanizing your offer can make it more relatable. One of the easiest ways to do this is using a relevant image.</span><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"> Images play a&#160; huge part in converting visitors. They’re the first thing that catches the their eye before they read the headline.</span></p>\n<p><a href=\"http://www.t-sciences.com/news/humans-process-visual-data-better\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noreferrer noopener\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Images are processed 60,000 times faster than text by the brain</span></a><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">, so what the visitor sees will influence their immediate opinions about your brand and offer.</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Like headlines, use imagery to grab attention. Make them relevant to your product or service.</span></p>\n<ul>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">If you’re offering a product, your imagery should be of the product</span></li>\n<li style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">If you’re offering a service, your imagery should relate to what the service is in a way that paints a positive picture in the mind of the user</span></li>\n</ul>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Remember that you don’t have long to make a good first impression. Make sure images are large and high-quality. Try to stay clear of stock imagery — you don’t want to show visitors something they may have already seen.</span></p>\n<h3><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Landing Page Image Example</span></h3>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\">Teambit is a great example of imagery done well — original illustrations used to capture attention and promote its service:</span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-weight: 400;\"><img class=\"alignnone wp-image-88754 size-full\" src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/02/Article-Image-5.jpg\" alt=\"landing page example with strong image example\" width=\"740\" height=\"409\"/></span></p>\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Talk up the benefits&#160;</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Let’s face it: the average attention span is shorter than ever – <a href=\"https://venturebeat.com/2016/12/04/our-8-second-attention-span-and-the-future-of-news-media/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer nofollow noopener\">eight seconds, to be exact</a>. So when you craft large blocks of text, you risk lower engagement and fewer conversions.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>As a result, you want to write copy that’s easily scannable and highlights the most important elements. This way, visitors can quickly determine whether your solution is right for their needs.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3} -->\n<h3>The Benefits of Opting-In Need To Be Clear</h3>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>When it comes to writing out the benefits of your offer, focus on clarity. Clearly explain how what you’re offering can solve the user’s problem. But do it in as few words as possible.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>According to <a href=\"https://www.marketingprofs.com/charts/2017/31924/lead-gen-landing-page-benchmarks-conversion-rates-and-content-metrics\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer nofollow noopener\">MarketingProfs</a>, landing pages with more than 800 words have a 33% lower conversion rate than pages with less than 200 words. Bullet points are a great way to keep things concise and make benefits easily digestible for the user.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Bullet points also allow you to use minimal text and draw attention because of the way they’re styled. And when you combine bullet points with white space you increase their effectiveness even more.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Establish your USP</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Your <a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/email-marketing/how-to-pinpoint-your-businesss-hook-find-your-unique-selling-proposition-in-6-simple-steps.htm?utm_source=awblog&#38;utm_medium=email&#38;utm_campaign=blogcontent&#38;utm_content=blogcontent021219webcom\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer nofollow noopener\">USP (Unique Selling Point)</a> is the thing that sets you apart from the competition and the reason why people will choose you over everyone else.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Studies show that you have <a href=\"http://time.com/12933/what-you-think-you-know-about-the-web-is-wrong/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer nofollow noopener\">less than 15 seconds</a> to capture someone’s attention when they land on your website. That’s how long they’ll stick around before deciding whether what you’re offering is right for them. So you need to impress them quickly.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3} -->\n<h3>What’s in a Value Proposition?</h3>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Value propositions include:</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:list -->\n<ul><li>Showing how your product or service compares against a well-known competitor</li><li>The ROI that can be achieved</li><li>The monetary value of the product and the saving that can be made by signing up now</li><li>The success that can be achieved</li><li>Making it clear that your offer is free</li><li>A guarantee</li></ul>\n<!-- /wp:list -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Define a strong, value-driven USP and build your landing page around it. You can complement your USP with strong headlines,images, and relevant copy.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>A value proposition is a key component of your <a href=\"https://www.web.com/blog/grow/marketing/guide-small-business-marketing\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer nofollow noopener\">small business marketing strategy</a>, and shows the user what they’ll gain when they take action, whether that is filling out a form or making a purchase.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3} -->\n<h3>Unique Value Proposition Landing Page Example</h3>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Airbnb does this brilliantly. Take a look at how it pairs its USP (earning money by renting a room in your home) with a value proposition (how much you could earn by becoming a host).</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:image {\"id\":88749} -->\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image\"><img src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/02/Article-Image-1.jpg\" alt=\"Example of a strong Unique Value Proposition page\" class=\"wp-image-88749\"/></figure>\n<!-- /wp:image -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Make calls-to-action strong and clear</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Every element of your landing page is designed to get visitors to notice and click on the call-to-action.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>The golden rules of form optimization are to keep it concise and feature a compelling, unique call-to-action.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>If your form is too long, you may scare visitors away because you’re requesting too much information. And if your Call-To-Action (CTA) isn’t personalized or it’s difficult to find, you jeopardize the chances of converting your visitor into a customer.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3} -->\n<h3>Standard Call-to-Action Rules</h3>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:list -->\n<ul><li>Make it big enough not to be missed</li><li>Always use a button. People are conditioned to expect a button, don’t throw a curveball at them</li><li>Use a contrasting color that attracts the eye</li><li>Use actionable words (e.g. “Get your Free Trial,” “Buy Now,” “Download Now,” etc.)</li></ul>\n<!-- /wp:list -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Powerful CTAs are an important part of successful landing pages. You don’t want to make visitors guess or even have to think deeply about an action. The CTA should be obvious and ready to capitalize on your desired action.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Depending on the length of the landing page, you may need to incorporate multiple CTAs throughout the content.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3} -->\n<h3>Call-to-Action Example</h3>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:image {\"id\":91774,\"sizeSlug\":\"full\"} -->\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-full\"><img src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/06_photo-summit-DESKTOP-e1595951927604.png\" alt=\"An example of a strong call to action button\" class=\"wp-image-91774\"/></figure>\n<!-- /wp:image -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Include contact information</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Contact information tells the visitor that you’re a real company. It lets them know that there’s someone behind the landing page, which increases trust.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Including a physical address and contact phone number is the most basic way of adding legitimacy. What those things don’t do, though, is encourage contact. If you want to be helpful to visitors, give them a way to get in touch online. There are three ways you can do this.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:list -->\n<ul><li>Include a chat pop-up that follows the visitor down the page, making you available to answer any questions</li><li>Include a contact form on the page</li><li>Include a contact call-to-action that clicks through to a dedicated contact page</li></ul>\n<!-- /wp:list -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Find an easy to use Landing Page Builder</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Once we lay out what it takes to create a high converting landing page, it sounds pretty easy.&#160; But if it doesn’t, don’t worry, plenty of small business owners either don’t have the time or know-how to create a website landing page to help create additional business opportunities.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Luckily, there are platforms available which make creating and optimizing your landing page super easy.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>AWeber’s Landing Page Builder will allow you to create visually stunning landing pages with our easy drag-and-drop editor. Want something even easier?&#160; No problem, your landing pages could be ready in minutes. Just choose any of the hundreds of landing page templates available. And the best part, they’re all free as part of AWeber Free.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:buttons {\"align\":\"center\"} -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-buttons aligncenter\"><!-- wp:button {\"textColor\":\"very-dark-gray\",\"customBackgroundColor\":\"#ffaf62\",\"borderRadius\":0,\"className\":\"is-style-fill\"} -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-button is-style-fill\"><a class=\"wp-block-button__link has-text-color has-very-dark-gray-color has-background no-border-radius\" href=\"https://www.aweber.com/free.htm?utm_source=awblog&#38;utm_medium=email&#38;utm_campaign=blogcontent&#38;utm_content=blogpost88746-landingpagetrial\" style=\"background-color:#ffaf62\">Get started with AWeber Free</a></div>\n<!-- /wp:button --></div>\n<!-- /wp:buttons -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3} -->\n<h3>AWeber Landing Page Template Examples</h3>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:image {\"align\":\"center\",\"id\":91990,\"sizeSlug\":\"large\"} -->\n<div class=\"wp-block-image\"><figure class=\"aligncenter size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2019/02/LP-Index-1-1024x714.jpg\" alt=\"AWeber's Landing Page Builder Template examples\" class=\"wp-image-91990\"/></figure></div>\n<!-- /wp:image -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Test, test, test</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Landing pages are trial and error. Once you’ve created a page you’re happy with, don’t put it live and just leave it. Always monitor performance. Look at your analytics weekly and look at performance over time. Use <a href=\"https://www.luckyorange.com/heat-maps.php\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer nofollow noopener\">heatmaps</a> and <a href=\"https://www.crazyegg.com/scrollmap\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer nofollow noopener\">scrollmaps</a> to see how people are interacting with the page and use the information to improve your landing pages performance.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>If your page isn’t bringing in the number of leads or conversions you expected, tweak elements of the design or copy, or tinker around with the color and positioning of buttons.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Then, run A/B tests to see how the different pages perform against one another. From there, you’ll be able to take the best elements of both to produce a page that gives you bang for your buck.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Use Search Engine Optimization to drive landing page traffic.</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Remember that your landing page is public, so it has the potential to be discovered by people who are typing specific search queries into a search engine such as Google. So make sure that you can maximize that public value by following some basic SEO strategies.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Make sure the page itself is <a rel=\"noreferrer nofollow noopener\" href=\"https://yoast.com/what-is-crawlability/\" target=\"_blank\">crawlable</a>, so you’re not blocking it from search in the robots.txt file or through noindex tags. You also want the page to have some clean HTML markup with crawlable text and a strong title tag, meta description and URL (some basic <a rel=\"noreferrer nofollow noopener\" href=\"https://support.google.com/webmasters/answer/35769?hl=en\" target=\"_blank\">guidelines from Google</a> for reference). Put the page into <a rel=\"noreferrer nofollow noopener\" href=\"https://adwords.google.com/KeywordPlanner\" target=\"_blank\">Google’s Keyword Planner</a> to get ideas for keywords you could incorporate into some of these elements. Run your email landing page through <a href=\"https://www.google.com/webmasters/tools/googlebot-fetch\">Googl</a><a href=\"https://www.google.com/webmasters/tools/googlebot-fetch\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer nofollow noopener\">e</a><a href=\"https://www.google.com/webmasters/tools/googlebot-fetch\"> Sea</a><a rel=\"noreferrer nofollow noopener\" href=\"https://www.google.com/webmasters/tools/googlebot-fetch\" target=\"_blank\">r</a><a href=\"https://www.google.com/webmasters/tools/googlebot-fetch\">ch Console</a> to check crawlability.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3} -->\n<h3>Establish Your Brand</h3>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Since visitors from organic search traffic may be completely unfamiliar with you, make sure that the landing page represents your brand in a meaningful way. You don’t need to sacrifice any specific language or design pieces; just make it easy for your page to live on its own and do more outside of the campaign.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Landing page content often has some extremely good value for <a href=\"https://yoast.com/focus-on-long-tail-keywords/#:~:text=Long%2Dtail%20keywords%20are%20keywords,as%20they%20are%20more%20specific.\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer nofollow noopener\">long-tail keywords</a>, so some basic landing page SEO can provide new traffic for a long time, providing extra value on top of your initial email landing page investment.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2><em>Conclusion</em></h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>As you optimize your landing page, be sure to reflect on what’s working and what isn’t. Then test new ideas and tactics to continue improving your conversion rates.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>And remember – once your prospects sign up for your product, service, or email list, the work isn’t over yet. It’s time to keep them engaged by sending related content offers, freebies and more through <a href=\"https://www.aweber.com/index.htm\">AWeber’s email marketing platform</a>.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Your landing page converting is a sign that it’s working, and people are putting their trust in you to deliver on what you say. Repay trust and reward loyalty by emailing customers with content that adds value, personalized offers, and freebies, or letting them know when they left items in their cart. <a href=\"https://www.wordstream.com/blog/ws/2017/06/29/email-marketing-statistics\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer nofollow noopener\">Every dollar spent on email marketing has an ROI of $44</a>. Once a person has opted-in to your email list, use it to your advantage.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><strong>Related:&#160;</strong><a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/email-marketing/how-to-get-your-first-50-email-subscribers-in-less-than-30-days.htm?utm_source=awblog&#38;utm_medium=email&#38;utm_campaign=blogcontent&#38;utm_content=blogcontent021219webcom\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">How to Get Your First 50 Email Subscribers in 30 Days</a></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Not sure what to include in your emails? <a href=\"https://www.aweber.com/whattowrite.htm?utm_source=awblog&#38;utm_medium=email&#38;utm_campaign=blogcontent&#38;utm_content=blogcontent021219webcomwtw\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Download 45+ free writing templates</a> to learn how to craft emails like a pro.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>About the author: With nearly a decade of digital marketing experience, Chandal has created content strategies for both the biggest and sometimes the most unexpected markets, while developing strategic relationships with editors and publishers.
