Or should I say, Hola! Bonjour! Konnichiwa!</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Email is global. As you set out to grow and engage your audience through email marketing, there’s no geographic limit to where someone could discover you and join your list.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Creating emails brimming with compelling content and engaging visuals is essential to a successful email marketing campaign. But what happens when the person reading your emails doesn’t speak the same language as you?</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Easily translate your emails into any language with Unicode</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Unicode is an international encoding standard that allows emails to be delivered to subscribers in different languages. The Unicode characters will allow your subscribers to read your content in their native language.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>When you write emails using Unicode characters, it becomes a lot easier to create messages that your customers and prospects can understand.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>&#160;If you have a subscriber that speaks a different language (such as Thai), they will be able to see Thai characters (such as ณ) in your message.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3} -->\n<h3>Example of a message in Thai</h3>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:image {\"id\":92292,\"sizeSlug\":\"large\"} -->\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Image-1-Email-in-Thai.png\" alt=\"Email message example in Thai\" class=\"wp-image-92292\"/></figure>\n<!-- /wp:image -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>If writing messages in a foreign language isn’t a concern for you, you may want to use Unicode to add symbols ( $↞ ) and emoticons (😻 🌞) to jazz up your messages. Because who doesn’t love a cat with strange heart eyes and smiling sun?</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3} -->\n<h3>Examples of using symbols and emoticons&#160;</h3>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:image {\"id\":92293,\"sizeSlug\":\"large\"} -->\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Image-2-Emojis-1024x404.png\" alt=\"Example of an email using emoticons and symbols.\" class=\"wp-image-92293\"/></figure>\n<!-- /wp:image -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Taking the time to send emails in your subscribers’ native language(s) shows that you value them.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Not only does this mean you can more clearly connect and communicate with your audience (or even reach new audiences), you’ve given your subscribers&#160; a reason to trust you more than ever before.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>That makes growing your email list and developing long-lasting relationships with your customers easy.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Breaking the language barrier</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>AWeber enables customers to send emails to their email marketing lists in any language using Unicode.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Here are four ways you can use foreign characters to better connect with your subscribers:</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3} -->\n<h3>1. Send segmented messages</h3>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:image -->\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image\"><img src=\"https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/pIDl8wbE5EarHV3A4AyKYyt4c0oLHl9tKyipHMUi5El2iuzS3bgUifx2OQoSjrL6jaPN8WbmFErrQ-b-qNrL4nU4645GVB9OjyvFdXuydV2UTSTEABNFMYfjH9YNDLI7DScSdQWJ\" alt=\"Segmented message in English, Spanish, German and French\"/></figure>\n<!-- /wp:image -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>If you have subscribers from various countries, you can make it easier for them to read your emails by <a href=\"https://help.aweber.com/hc/en-us/articles/204253268-What-Type-Of-Characters-Can-I-Use-In-My-Messages-\">sending targeted emails in their native language(s)</a>. When they can read your message in their native language, it’ll help create a more positive experience for your customers and prospects.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Removing language barriers between you and your subscribers also eliminates the possibility of miscommunication. Instead of leaving it up to your subscribers to translate your message, they’re able to understand you immediately.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>And when your audience has a clear understanding of the value your products/services will bring to them, they’ll be in a better position to make a purchase.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><strong>Pro Tip: </strong>Add international keyboards (if you haven’t already) to your computer to easily create new email messages in different languages.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3} -->\n<h3>2. Personalize your bilingual emails</h3>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:image -->\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image\"><img src=\"https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/Rb7TDMxjj_iXiDggg0g8Z-hcd1-Wzhz-qPEc1jhrTMtj-l4qescptKEdBVsQfKPJ6J7m3I1glnucT1qL1uagig0ZqBPatG1VHxvnWsnrvoShnhQPDZjpQsuQa7nbuJeKmbauGguq\" alt=\"personalized emails\"/></figure>\n<!-- /wp:image -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>It’s frustrating when you want to send a personalized email to your subscribers, only to discover that a character in their name isn’t supported and, consequently, doesn’t display correctly. And if you can’t do this for every single subscriber, it becomes difficult to do it at all.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Fortunately,<a href=\"https://help.aweber.com/hc/en-us/articles/204847177-Which-Character-Set-Do-AWeber-Forms-Accept-\"> AWeber sign up forms use UTF-8</a> (the character encoding system that stores and displays Unicode characters correctly).&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>AWeber sign up forms accept Unicode characters, which allows your subscribers to enter characters in their native language. So if you have a subscriber that speaks a different language (such as Thai), they will be able to enter their information in your form using characters (such as ณ) from that language.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><strong>Pro Tip</strong>: <a href=\"https://help.aweber.com/hc/en-us/articles/204029906-What-Can-I-Personalize-in-My-Messages-\">Add “First Name” custom fields</a> to your subject lines and/or within your email messages to grab your subscribers’ attention and create a more individualized experience.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3} -->\n<h3>3. Send Confirmation Opt-In messages in 19 different languages&#160;</h3>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Already know that your target audience primarily speaks a specific language? By greeting your subscribers in their own language, you can increase the conversion rate of confirmations and kick off a lasting relationship with your new prospects and customers.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Confirmed opt-in is one of the best ways to protect your list against unwarranted SPAM complaints, malicious sign ups, and it helps to keep the unsubscribe rate low.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>If you know your audience will prefer a specific language, select that language to provide more clarity on how they can confirm their email address. By greeting your subscribers in their own language, you can increase the conversion rate of confirmations and kick off a lasting relationship with your new prospects and customers.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>These are the language options that are currently available:</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:list -->\n<ul><li>Chinese (Simplified)</li><li>Chinese (Traditional)</li><li>Danish</li><li>Dutch</li><li>English</li><li>French</li><li>German</li><li>Indonesian</li><li>Italian</li><li>Japanese</li><li>Korean</li><li>Malay</li><li>Norwegian</li><li>Polish</li><li>Portuguese</li><li>Russian</li><li>Slovenian</li><li>Spanish</li><li>Swedish</li></ul>\n<!-- /wp:list -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3} -->\n<h3>How to easily change your language selection</h3>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>To change the confirmation message language for an active list, select List Settings in the List Options dropdown of your account.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:image {\"id\":92294,\"sizeSlug\":\"large\"} -->\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Image-6-List-Settings-1024x380.png\" alt=\"AWeber dashboard highlighting list setting.\" class=\"wp-image-92294\"/></figure>\n<!-- /wp:image -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Choose Confirmation Message on the left-hand menu, and in the Language section, select the language that meets your needs.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:image {\"id\":92295,\"sizeSlug\":\"large\"} -->\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Image-7-Languages-1024x728.png\" alt=\"AWeber dashboard highlighting how language is selected.\" class=\"wp-image-92295\"/></figure>\n<!-- /wp:image -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3} -->\n<h3>Example of French language confirmation message</h3>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:image {\"id\":92297,\"sizeSlug\":\"large\"} -->\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/Image-8-Confirmation-Message-French-679x1024.png\" alt=\"Example of French confirmation message.\" class=\"wp-image-92297\"/></figure>\n<!-- /wp:image -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>When you select a language, the header, body, and signature of the confirmation message will automatically update.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>All approved subject lines will be translated. If you are using a custom one, you will need to translate it directly.&#160;&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><strong>Pro Tip</strong>: If you’re not sure what language your subscribers prefer, consider surveying them.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3} -->\n<h3>4. Send international emails in two or more languages.</h3>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>You can create a separate email in each language or you can use dynamic content. <a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/email-marketing/aweber-dynamic-email-content-feature.htm\">Dynamic content</a> changes based on the viewer’s criteria. Often most people only use dynamic content to personalize a greeting. By adding a personalization snippet after the greeting like&#160; — ‘Hello {{subscriber.first_name}}’</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>But you can use dynamic content for multi-language campaigns, if you know your individual subscriber’s preferred language or their IP address.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3} -->\n<h3>Set up dynamic content for different languages</h3>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Let's say that you have an email campaign, and you know your subscribers' native language is either English, French, or Spanish. You could create three emails in each of those native languages. Or use dynamic content to create just <em>one email</em>, making the content in your email dynamic, so each recipient receives an email in his or her own native language.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>You will need to segment your list by assigning tags to identify the subscriber's native language. Get this information by asking them their preference with an AWeber landing page, sign up form, or a survey.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><strong>Pro Tip:</strong> Where there are cases in which you cannot identify a recipient’s country/language, he or she will receive the email in English by default.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>To make this process easier, AWeber automatically lists the location where the subscriber signed up. For example, if the subscriber lives in a known Spanish-speaking country, you could assign a Spanish tag since that is the native language.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3} -->\n<h3>How to use dynamic content for native languages</h3>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Dynamic content is a combination of a default version of the text and variants for every other language that you support.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Not fluent in the language you want to send? Put your copy into <a href=\"http://translate.google.com/translate?\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Google translate</a> to receive a language translation.&#160;&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>One word of warning: Google Translate is not always perfect. It is a decent option if you are not fluent or don’t have the resources to hire a translator.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Once you have the translation, then you simply add some conditional content language for each text section.&#160; Just make sure your&#160; have a language tag assigned to your subscribers.&#160;&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>If your subscriber has the language tag “fr” the french version would appear. If their language tag is “es” the spanish version would appear.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Here’s how you would write the dynamic logic markup would look like to add conditional content in the greeting.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><strong>{% if “fr” in subscriber.tags %}</strong></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Bonjour...</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><strong>{% elseif '\"es\" in subscriber.tags %}</strong></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Hola...</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><strong>{% else %}</strong></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Hello...</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><strong>{% endif %}</strong></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>You would repeat the process&#160; above for each text section. If you interested in learning more about adding dynamic logic into your emails, AWeber has step-by-step guides on how to add <a href=\"https://help.aweber.com/hc/en-us/articles/360036633074-What-is-Dynamic-Email-Content-\">conditional content logic markup</a>.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>“I can't think of a nicer gesture than making sure each of your subscribers receives your email written in their own native language,” says Email Delivery Product Manager Dave Stys.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Tips for sending emails in the most common languages we see in AWeber</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3} -->\n<h3>3 tips for sending emails in French</h3>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>In France, there is more formality when addressing others than in the United States. While you can always send the same translated content to your French-speaking subscribers, you may want to make a few minor adjustments.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:list {\"ordered\":true} -->\n<ol><li><strong>Use the proper greeting and close</strong>. If you collect your subscriber's first and last name, consider taking an extra step to send a greeting using their last name versus first name. Include the appropriate prefixes: Mr., Mrs., and Miss. Note: There is no French equivalent for the prefix Ms. and in 2012 the France Prime Minister <a href=\"https://www.frenchtoday.com/blog/french-culture/madame-or-mademoiselle-a-delicate-question/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">banned the use of Mademoiselle</a> in legal documents, so Mademoiselle is less frequently used.&#160;</li><li><strong>Write a concise, and descriptive subject line</strong>. When you test subject lines, you will most likely find a <a href=\"https://www.validity.com/who-does-email-really-well-in-france/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">shorter, concise, and descriptive subject line</a> has a higher open rate for your French readers.</li><li><strong>Structure your email with clear sentences that identify the value.</strong> Your french readers will be receptive to sentences that clearly outline the value and the benefits. Keep in mind that the value can take a variety of forms: financial (free delivery, a coupon for a discount), convenience (auto-shipments, electronic receipts, track shipment notices), or information (recipes, free additional content, how-to tutorial).&#160; &#160;</li></ol>\n<!-- /wp:list -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3} -->\n<h3>3 tips for sending emails in Spanish</h3>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>You may not want to limit sending Spanish emails just outside of the United States. If you have an extensive subscriber base in California, Texas, and Florida, it may be worthwhile surveying your customers on how many speak Spanish since these three states <a href=\"https://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2017/10/31/use-of-spanish-declines-among-latinos-in-major-u-s-metros/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">include 57% of Spanish-speaking Latinos in the U.S.</a></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>If you have a large number of subscribers who speak Spanish, you may want to identify your Spanish speakers and give them the option to receive your content in English or Spanish. There are 57 million Latinos in the United States, and the U.S. Hispanic population is expected to grow to one-quarter of the total U.S. population by 2050.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:list {\"ordered\":true} -->\n<ol><li><strong>Consider an alternate content presentation. </strong>The Spanish language has a more persuasive style and argument structure, so consider altering how you typically deliver content if you create a Spanish version. To get your point across, lead with the emotion and the why of your product versus an analytical approach.&#160;</li><li><strong>Know your audience's market and how Spanish is used</strong>. There is no \"typical\" Hispanic customer, so try to learn as much about your audience as possible, like education, country of origin, and geographic location. A <a href=\"https://www.pewresearch.org/fact-tank/2017/10/31/use-of-spanish-declines-among-latinos-in-major-u-s-metros/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Pew study </a>identified that Spanish-speaking markets vary drastically on a city-by-city basis. For example, 90 percent of Latinos speak Spanish at home in Miami, FL, and McAllen, TX. Other major markets with Spanish-speaking populations of 79 percent or above include El Paso, Los Angeles, New York, Atlanta, Dallas, and Orlando.</li><li><strong>Simply translating English to Spanish may not be enough. </strong>Most Hispanic marketing experts have found that translating content from English to Spanish alone is not enough to have an effective campaign. You may want to invest in a copywriter fluent in Spanish and familiar with the Spanish culture to guide you on cultural references and nuances. But it may be well worth the effort, a \"<a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/business/news/insights/gains-in-translation-what-your-language-choices-say-to-us-hispanics\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Facebook IQ</a>\" study conducted by Latinum Network found:</li></ol>\n<!-- /wp:list -->\n\n<!-- wp:list -->\n<ul><li>When online, more than 80% of Spanish-dominant Hispanics use Spanish at least half of the time when they read, write, or watch videos.</li><li>&#160;79% of Spanish-dominant, 82% of bilingual, and 60% of English-dominant Hispanics surveyed think brands should reach out to consumers in both English and Spanish.</li><li>58% of Spanish-dominant Hispanics and 48% of bilingual Hispanics believe that brands that reach out in Spanish demonstrate they value the Hispanic community.</li></ul>\n<!-- /wp:list -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>A note before you send</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>You can’t copy and paste foreign characters from an outside service like Microsoft Word. Your content must be created within the email to guarantee language support.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Getting started</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Sending emails to subscribers in their native languages is a simple way to improve the communication between you and your customers and create an enjoyable brand experience.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>If you have any questions about sending international emails, don’t hesitate to reach out to our <a href=\"https://www.aweber.com/contact-us.htm?utm_source=awblog&#38;utm_medium=email&#38;utm_campaign=product&#38;utm_content=foreignlanguages\">award-winning customer solutions team</a>.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2><a href=\"https://www.aweber.com/free-email-marketing.htm?utm_source=awblog&#38;utm_medium=email&#38;utm_campaign=product&#38;utm_content=foreignlanguages\">Best free email marketing software</a></h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Our mission is simple: to deliver powerfully-simple email marketing tools to help small business owners and entrepreneurs — like you — grow your business.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>AWeber Free is our completely free email marketing and landing pages plan — perfect for those who are just getting started or kicking off a passion project. -->\n<p>What do successful marketing strategies and breakfast have in common?&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Answer: The best ones involve variety.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Think about it. A healthy breakfast means eating a variety of foods — fruit, toast, eggs. You need a variety of foods with different nutrients to fuel your body and stay healthy.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>A <a href=\"https://www.thebalancesmb.com/how-to-write-a-small-business-marketing-plan-2951749\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">healthy marketing plan</a> needs variety, too. To be successful with marketing, you need to use different tactics and test strategies to find what works for your business. You can’t go all in on one thing, and one thing <em>only</em>.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Side note</em>: if you hear “this is the only tool you need,” turn and run the other way. Always be skeptical of tools or strategies that promise it all. Small business influencer Rieva Lesonsky talks about this more on <a href=\"https://www.aweber.com/podcast.htm\">The FWD: Thinking Show.</a>&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>So what can you do to diversify your marketing strategy?&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Enter: web push notifications. Not only do push notifications let you communicate updates to your audience, they enable you to drive traffic to your website or landing page, build your audience, and grow your business. Plus, they work great in tandem with email marketing.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Read on to learn all about web push notifications and how you can use them to complement your marketing strategy.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>What are web push notifications?</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Web push notifications — also known as desktop notifications or simply push notifications — are short, one-time messages that are delivered straight to a subscriber’s desktop when they have a browser open.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Web push notifications are sent to people who have opted-in to receive messages from you. Once they’ve opted-in, subscribers do not have to be on your website in order to receive a push notification.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>They usually appear in a corner of your desktop or laptop screen and serve to alert your audience of exclusive deals, offers, promotions, or even freebies.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>The goal of push notifications is to drive your audience back to your website or landing page and take the action you want them to take.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:image {\"id\":92747,\"sizeSlug\":\"large\"} -->\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/WPN-Cover-1024x597.png\" alt=\"Where web push notifications appear on a desktop screen.\" class=\"wp-image-92747\"/><figcaption>Web push notifications usually appear in the top right corner of your desktop screen.</figcaption></figure>\n<!-- /wp:image -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3} -->\n<h3>What’s the difference between a web push notification, an in-browser notification, and a mobile push notification?</h3>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>An in-browser notification is another form of online messaging that targets active website visitors when they are actively on your website.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Mobile push notifications are the types of notifications that appear on a mobile device. These messages go to a user’s phone and show up on a lock screen. When a user opens a push notification, it will bring the user to whatever app sent the message. Much like web push notifications, users can opt-in and opt-out of receiving notifications.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>But in this guide, we’ll be covering all you need to know about web push notifications. They differ from in-browser notifications and mobile push notifications in that a user does not need to be on the website in order to receive the push notification. This allows marketers to reach users when they’re not actively engaging on a website.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Why marketers should use web push notifications</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Marketers use web push notifications to build, inform, and retain their audience. Web push notifications capture subscribers’ attention, no matter what they’re doing online.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Whether a person is in their email inbox, scrolling social media, or browsing their favorite ecommerce sites, if they are subscribed to your opt-in messages, they will receive them.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>And the stats speak for themselves. <a href=\"https://www.digitalmarketer.com/blog/web-push-notification-metrics-to-optimize/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">DigitalMarketer</a> analyzed web push notification metrics and found they maintain a click through rate of 4-6% even when subscriber count is above 25,000. </p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Web push notifications also offer marketers a more flexible form of communication, allowing subscribers to opt-in and opt-out with more freedom than a typical full page popup <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Modal_window\" target=\"_blank\">modal</a>.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>There are three primary reasons why marketers use web push notifications to elevate their marketing strategy.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:list {\"ordered\":true} -->\n<ol><li><strong>To inform. </strong>Web push notifications are a great way to keep subscribers in the loop with exclusive content, offers, deals and more. Ultimately, subscribers can’t take action if they’re not aware of special deals or new content that you want to send out on push notifications.</li></ol>\n<!-- /wp:list -->\n\n<!-- wp:list {\"ordered\":true,\"start\":2} -->\n<ol start=\"2\"><li><strong>To engage. </strong>Web push notifications provide a unique opportunity for users to engage with your brand, even when they’re not actively on your website.&#160;</li></ol>\n<!-- /wp:list -->\n\n<!-- wp:list {\"ordered\":true,\"start\":3} -->\n<ol start=\"3\"><li><strong>To sell. </strong>Capitalize on subscribers being on their desktop to let them know about an exclusive offer. You never know what they might be looking for online and if you can provide it for them, a push notification is a simple, straightforward way to communicate your value.&#160;</li></ol>\n<!-- /wp:list -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>What do push notifications look like?</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>While simple in design and layout, these push notifications pack a powerful punch in a little package.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:image {\"id\":92749,\"sizeSlug\":\"large\"} -->\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image size-large\"><img src=\"https://blog.aweber.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/08/WPN-Anatomy-1-1-1024x480.png\" alt=\"The anatomy of a web push notification\" class=\"wp-image-92749\"/><figcaption>The anatomy of a web push notification</figcaption></figure>\n<!-- /wp:image -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>As you can see from the image above, there are 4 components of a web push notification — let’s break them down.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><strong>A.</strong> <strong>Logo. </strong>Including a brand logo on a web push notification provides instant recognition from a user. It’s a highly visual way for a subscriber to recognize that the message is coming from your brand, and can drive them to read the notification and take action</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><strong>B.</strong> <strong>Title. </strong>The title of the web push notification is also called the header text. This is the piece of text that will catch the attention of a subscriber and decide to read on.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><strong>C.</strong> <strong>Message. </strong>This vital section is where you can elaborate your message. This is your opportunity to concisely explain the value a subscriber receives from clicking on your push notification and visiting your site. Answer questions like: what will your subscribers receive by visiting your site? How long will the offer last? Keep in mind, however, that web push notifications are meant to be short and sweet.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><strong>D.</strong> <strong>Domain. </strong>This is the URL that the user subscribed to. Including the source link in your message can’t be changed. It not only serves to remind the subscriber of your website, but aids in recognition and awareness of your online presence.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>How to use push notifications in your marketing strategy</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Now that you know the basics about web push notifications and the benefit of using them, let’s get into how to use push notifications as a part of your broader marketing strategy.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3} -->\n<h3>Getting started with push notifications as a marketing tactic</h3>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>When considering web push notifications as part of your broader marketing strategy, there’s a few things you want to consider:</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:list {\"ordered\":true} -->\n<ol><li><strong>Align your strategy with your business goals.</strong></li></ol>\n<!-- /wp:list -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Is your goal to get more website traffic? Do you want to make more sales? Drive visitors to view new content or sign up for a guide? </p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Whatever your business goals are, consider how web push notifications can support them. This will help you figure out what kind of messages you want to send out to your audience.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:list {\"ordered\":true,\"start\":2} -->\n<ol start=\"2\"><li><strong>Think about the user experience.&#160;</strong></li></ol>\n<!-- /wp:list -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>When a website visitor signs up to receive your push notifications, what will they experience? Where do you want to take them? What actions do you want them to take? How will you control the message and make sure they’re receiving value?</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:list {\"ordered\":true,\"start\":3} -->\n<ol start=\"3\"><li><strong>Use push notifications in tandem with other marketing tactics.&#160;</strong></li></ol>\n<!-- /wp:list -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Make sure that push notifications fit in with how you’re marketing your business across all your marketing channels. You may have heard this described as <a href=\"https://econsultancy.com/what-is-cross-channel-marketing-and-why-do-you-need-it/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">cross-channel marketing</a>, or omnichannel marketing.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>This means that people experience the brand consistently across different marketing channels, which is why maintaining a consistent brand voice and branding is key.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>But why is this so important? According to <a href=\"https://www.clickz.com/onmichannel-marketing-automation-statistics-for-2019/231381-2/231381/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">ClickZ</a>, customers bought 250% more frequently when interacting with three or more channels than customers who only engaged with one channel.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Let’s get into this deeper and look at how you can use push notifications along with email marketing in your strategy.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3} -->\n<h3>How to use web push notifications and email marketing together</h3>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Web push notifications and email marketing support each other in many ways.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>While your email subscribers and your web push notification subscribers are independent of one another — meaning those who sign up for your email list don’t automatically become web push notification subscribers, and vice versa — you can drive subscribers of one to become subscribers of the other.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Let’s break down how to grow your web push notification subscribers using your email list.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":4} -->\n<h4>Step 1: Write the Opt-In Prompt</h4>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>In order to start collecting web push notification subscribers, you need to ask your website visitors if they’d like to subscribe to receive notifications from you.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>That initial ask is called the opt-in prompt. The goal of the opt-in prompt is to encourage website visitors to allow you to send them push notifications to their desktop.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Writing a compelling opt-in prompt begins by explaining what a subscriber will receive from you. This offer has to be valuable to the reader in order for them to let you send them notifications.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":4} -->\n<h4>Step 2: Ask your email list to subscribe to your web push notifications</h4>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Alert email subscribers about opting in to receive your push notifications. This is called the ‘soft ask’ and explains the value of opting-in to receive push notifications.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>An email subscriber may want to opt-in to receive push notifications for numerous reasons. Some of the more common reasons are that they want...</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:list -->\n<ul><li>A chance to receive exclusive offers and deals online.</li><li>Up-to-the-minute notifications about new blog posts, podcast episodes, social media posts, or other types of content.</li><li>To stay in touch with you.</li></ul>\n<!-- /wp:list -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Once you make the soft ask, drive email subscribers to your website to sign up via your opt-in prompt.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":4} -->\n<h4>Step 3: Create and send your web push notification</h4>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Once you’ve begun collecting web push notification subscribers, it’s time to send out your first notification.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Think about what action you want your subscribers to take back on your website. Do you want them to sign up for a webinar? Make a purchase? Download a guide or checklist? Whatever your lead magnet is that you want to promote will dictate the content that you send out.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>No matter what action you’re pushing your subscribers to do, here are a few tactics that will incite action:</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:list {\"ordered\":true} -->\n<ol><li><a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/email-marketing/how-to-create-a-lead-magnet.htm\"><strong>Create lead magnets</strong></a><strong> that speak to the pain points of your audience. </strong>Rule #1 of effective marketing is to know your audience and their pain points. Once you have a solid understanding of their needs and why they’re coming to you for help, you can create lead magnets that are tailored to solve their problems.&#160;</li></ol>\n<!-- /wp:list -->\n\n<!-- wp:list {\"ordered\":true,\"start\":2} -->\n<ol start=\"2\"><li><strong>Use FOMO</strong>. FOMO — or fear of missing out — creates a sense of urgency among your subscribers. If you have something truly amazing to offer your subscribers, most of them won’t want to miss the opportunity to take advantage.&#160;</li></ol>\n<!-- /wp:list -->\n\n<!-- wp:list {\"ordered\":true,\"start\":3} -->\n<ol start=\"3\"><li><strong>Make them feel special. </strong>Give your subscribers exclusive offers or content that no one else has access to. Not only does this make them more inclined to sign up initially via the opt-in prompt, it will keep them engaged and interested whenever you send out a push notification.</li></ol>\n<!-- /wp:list -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Once you’ve written an informative, engaging push notification that drives them to a desired location, it’s time to press “send.”</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":4} -->\n<h4>Step 4: Take your strategy to the next level.&#160;</h4>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Finally, consider where you're sending your web push notification subscribers in your messages.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>With a tool like AWeber, you can <a href=\"https://www.aweber.com/landing-page-builder.htm\">create a landing page</a> that promotes your business or your lead magnet. This is perfect especially if you don’t have a website, or you want to save on costs to build your own website.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Landing pages drive visitors to take one, specific action, which keeps web push notification subscribers on task and focused on the action you want them to take. Include a sign up form and the benefits a subscriber receives when they join your email list.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Plus, <a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/email-marketing/23-ways-to-tag-and-segment-your-subscribers-in-aweber.htm\">add a tag</a> to people who sign up for your email list via your landing page according to the lead magnet they signed up for. This lets you send personalized and tailored email content in the future if you wish.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Have you incorporated web push notifications into your marketing strategy?</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Then we’d love to hear from you! Post about your experience in the comments.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:html -->\n<script type=\"application/ld+json\">\n{\n  \"@context\": \"https://schema.org\",\n  \"@type\": \"FAQPage\",\n  \"mainEntity\": [{\n    \"@type\": \"Question\",\n    \"name\": \"What are web push notifications?\",\n    \"acceptedAnswer\": {\n      \"@type\": \"Answer\",\n      \"text\": \"Web push notifications are short, one-time messages that are delivered straight to a subscriber’s desktop when they have a browser open.\"\n    }\n  },{\n    \"@type\": \"Question\",\n    \"name\": \"Why marketers should use web push notifications?\",\n    \"acceptedAnswer\": {\n      \"@type\": \"Answer\",\n      \"text\": \"Marketers use web push notifications to build, inform, and retain their audience. DKIM","link":"https://blog.aweber.com/?p=91651","description":"<p><img width=\"1200\" height=\"675\" srcset=\"http://6elrmjmsbs335jwbeybarrry.wpengine.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/email-deliverability-best-practices-dkim_featured-social-1200x628-1.jpg 1200w, http://6elrmjmsbs335jwbeybarrry.wpengine.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/email-deliverability-best-practices-dkim_featured-social-1200x628-1-300x169.jpg 300w, http://6elrmjmsbs335jwbeybarrry.wpengine.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/email-deliverability-best-practices-dkim_featured-social-1200x628-1-768x432.jpg 768w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 1200px) 100vw, 1200px\" /></p><!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Getting into the inbox is the foundation of successful email marketing. You can spend hours crafting the perfect message, but if it goes to the spam folder, your subscriber won’t see it.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Mailbox providers (Gmail, Yahoo, and others) are always looking for ways to make the email they place in their customers’ inboxes more relevant. With the ever-increasing amount of emails being sent each day, the filters and systems they have in place are more advanced than ever, and are evolving continuously.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>To get into the inbox, you first need to follow fundamental email deliverability best practices:</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:list -->\n<ul><li>Only send email to people who have asked to receive it.</li><li>Make your content relevant, well-designed, and engaging.</li><li>Don’t send people content they are not expecting.</li><li>Don’t send more email to a person than they can easily read, and don’t send so little that they forget about you.</li></ul>\n<!-- /wp:list -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>If you have these best practices covered, then read on to find out how to supercharge your emails’ performance with DKIM.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Making your emails stand out</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Imagine a large, fast-flowing river. It’s autumn, so there are leaves floating down the river. I ask you to jump into the river and get me a leaf with my name written on it that fell from a specific tree. Now imagine that there are billions of leaves in the river. </p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>This is like what mailbox providers do every day to place emails into their customers’ inboxes.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Given this, when mailbox providers receive a message they attempt to identify who sent it, which allows them to treat emails from them as a group. Note, though, that doesn’t guarantee that every email will have the exact same outcome.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>This identification goes beyond just looking at the sending email address; behind the scenes there are email authentication standards in use that senders can take advantage of to ensure that their emails are grouped correctly and that they stand out from the crowd.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Giving your emails authentication superpowers</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Want to give your emails that extra effort to improve your email deliverability? Then setting up your DKIM is a must email deliverability best practice.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>So what is DKIM?</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/DomainKeys_Identified_Mail\" target=\"_blank\">DKIM</a> is an email authentication technology that helps stop <a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Spoofing_attack\" target=\"_blank\">spoofed</a> emails. It also connects domains in the email to the email message in a strong way that mailbox providers pay attention to. In other words, it makes an email “leaf” stand out in that proverbial large river.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:image -->\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image\"><img src=\"https://lh4.googleusercontent.com/E2y4OJoRIyYRhdt1m03bIwt_IeE4P8uh47qvV-AqxBJFCHeUKxji5DqF78S2LUERm-o_62dww1yr2-DNdivECvc5f_tWYGLZo2UofL5080XxqcYqwID7bg36Fj7iUF8fuJ_6bMTe\" alt=\"Illustration of the DKIM authentication process overview\"/></figure>\n<!-- /wp:image -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>You benefit from DKIM when you use it to connect your sending domain to the emails you send. This is what our <a href=\"https://help.aweber.com/hc/en-us/articles/360023682313-how-do-i-set-up-dkim-and-spf-records-for-my-domain-?utm_source=awblog&#38;utm_medium=email&#38;utm_campaign=product&#38;utm_content=dkim\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Custom DKIM</a> feature does, which gives you:</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:list -->\n<ul><li>A strong connection to your brand</li><li>A positive signal to mailbox providers</li><li>Allows you to to reap the full benefit of all of the hard work you put into making your emails perfect</li></ul>\n<!-- /wp:list -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Custom DKIM also gives you access to cool <a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/email-marketing/5-ridiculously-cool-ways-weve-used-amp-for-email.htm?utm_source=awblog&#38;utm_medium=email&#38;utm_campaign=product&#38;utm_content=dkim\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">AMP4Email features</a> which you can use to make your email content dynamic and more engaging!</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>How to set up Custom DKIM with AWeber</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:image -->\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image\"><img set up Custom DKIM\"/></figure>\n<!-- /wp:image -->\n\n<!-- wp:list {\"ordered\":true} -->\n<ol><li>Add your domain to your AWeber account and verify ownership of your sending email Rates with 22 of the best email subject lines\" srcset=\"http://6elrmjmsbs335jwbeybarrry.wpengine.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/blog-cover-1200x675-–-no-text.png 1200w, -->\n<p>If you’ve ever sat down to write an email, you’ve probably asked yourself: “what if no one opens my email?”&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Not a fun feeling, right? Especially if you’re worried that the success of your email rides entirely on your subject line. It’s basically <em>the thing </em>that will make subscribers want to open your message. </p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Thankfully, there are formulas to help make writing the best email subject lines as easy as pie.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>These 22 subject line formulas will help you write catchy subject lines that make subscribers eager to open your emails in no time.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Descriptive subject line formulas</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>The best email subject lines give your subscribers instant value. How? Tell your subscribers exactly what they can expect from your email using just your subject line.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>[Number] ways/strategies to [desired end goal]</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Example: 10 ways to get more email subscribers</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>[Desired end goal] without ever [negative feeling]</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Example: Lose weight without ever feeling hungry</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>How to [desired end goal] even if [barrier to accomplish desired end goal]</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Example: How to design a website even if you don’t have coding skills</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>[Action verb] with/by [lead magnet]</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Example: Kickstart your business with our Ultimate Guide to Email Marketing</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>[Desired end goal] with/by only [plan/strategy to reach desired outcome]</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Example: Get a job by only networking on LinkedIn</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Want more [desirable outcome] and less [undesirable outcome]?</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Example: Want more time and less stress?</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Short subject line formulas</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Want to stand out in the inbox? Then a shorter subject line may be the best strategy.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>On average, there are about<a rel=\"noreferrer noopener\" href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/email-marketing/how-long-should-my-email-subject-line-be.htm\" target=\"_blank\"> 44 characters in an email subject line.</a> Plus, mobile devices tend to cut subject lines off around 33-43 characters. If you want to make sure your subject line is fully visible — no matter how or when your subscriber receives your message — the best email subject lines may be short.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Get rid of [pain point] forever</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Example: Get rid of sleepless nights forever.</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>[Action/plan/method]. Here’s why/how</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Example: A/B test your videos. Here’s how</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>New [content]</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Example 1: New guide!&#160;</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Example 2: New arrival: check it out</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>[Number] recommended [product] for you</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Example: 7 Recommended homes for you</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Personalized subject line formulas</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Plus, don’t overlook the power of personalization. <a href=\"https://www.yesmarketing.com/who-we-are/news-and-events/news/data-personalized-email-subject-lines-boost-open-rates-50-percent\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Personalized email subject lines have been shown to boost open rates by 50%</a>. That’s because email subscribers want messages that feel personal and tailored to them.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Ready for [event/season/life event], [first name]?</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Example: Ready for Summer, Kelly?&#160;</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>[First name], your free [product] is waiting for you</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Example: Kelly, your free gift is waiting for you</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Hey, [first name], we have an offer for you…</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Hey, Kelly, we have an offer just for you...</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Subject line examples with emojis</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/email-marketing/2019-email-marketing-statistics.htm\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Only 6.9% of emails contain emojis.</a> That means an emoji could help your message stand out in a crowded inbox — as long as it’s relevant and used with a purpose.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>In fact, one study found that — when used correctly — <a href=\"https://www.mobilemarketer.com/news/study-emoji-drive-open-rates-for-push-notifications-254/527909/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">email messages that contain emojis in subject lines are opened 66% more than those without.</a>&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Sounds promising, right? As with anything in marketing, you’ll want to test emojis in your subject lines to see if they resonate with your audience. You might be surprised.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Here are some subject line examples that use emojis effectively.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:image Cookies using cookie emojis in its subject line\" width=\"580\" height=\"23\"/></figure>\n<!-- /wp:image -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Don't forget about preheaders</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/email-marketing/email-preheader.htm\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Email preheaders are a powerful tool to increase email open rates</a>. Not only do well-written preheaders give your subscribers more context for the email message, but creative preheaders can help give your email more personality.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Subject line: [Ask a question]</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Preheader: Here’s how</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Example:&#160;</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Subject line: Want to make more sales without spending hours prospecting?</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Preheader: Here’s how</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Subject line: [Product] is almost sold out</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Preheader: Get it before it’s gone</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Example:&#160;</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Subject line: Protein cupcakes are almost sold out!</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Preheader: Get ‘em before they’re gone.&#160;</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Subject line: [Case study] did [desired end goal]</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Preheader: And you can, too!</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Example:&#160;</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Subject line: This entrepreneur launched a business in 1 week</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Preheader: And you can, too!</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>E-Commerce subject line inspiration</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Drive more sales by trying out email subject lines that educate your audience about your product and promotions.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>It’s/They’re here! [New product], just for you</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Example headline: It’s here! New book releases, just for you</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Buy 1 [product], get 1 free</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Example: Buy 1 skirt, get 1 free</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Last chance to save [discount] on [product]</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Example: Last chance to save 30% off flights</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Your [discount/offer] ends [time period]</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><em>Example: Your 25% discount ends at midnight</em></p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>The one word subject line strategy</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>It’s hard to call a one word subject line a formula. But, yes, you can send subject lines with just one word. Nothing incites curiosity quite like a vague, but relevant, subject line.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Let’s look at a one word subject line example:</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:image {\"width\":500,\"height\":28} -->\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image is-resized\"><img src=\"https://lh6.googleusercontent.com/JXWNgBjnEa0vw0BvY1C9TUliN_Mwl5B6vjjVWL4KFOo6vgMqP21oCuK2Ue4WuDCpbAK5IUrdXkJy-uooy1MIMFXYt4CXcvf0wxyPiBPO0r_FNS_aHTBEOx9SCALZs5rKy1bZaUXx\" alt=\"One word email subject line example \" width=\"500\" height=\"28\"/></figure>\n<!-- /wp:image -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Thanks to genius use of pre-header text, we know there’s a big clearance sale. But this simple, one word subject line makes the reader interested. Don’t you want to see what all the fuss is about?&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>This strategy is useful if your goal is to drive traffic back to your website, too. In fact, <a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/email-marketing/this-email-split-test-increased-website-traffic-by-83.htm\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">one entrepreneur increased his website traffic by 83% using a one word email subject line</a> that hinted at the email contents.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Now that’s impressive.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Writing effective subject lines is an art and a science.&#160;</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>These email subject line formulas are meant to inspire you and help you think about your approach to writing. But don’t be afraid to experiment and try out some creative writing of your own.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Our best advice? Get creative! Try out different subject lines and test them to see what works for your audience.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>And if you need more guidance, <a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/email-marketing/your-guide-to-writing-the-worlds-best-email-subject-lines.htm\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">remember these 7 rules for writing the world’s best subject lines</a>.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Ready to boost your open rates?</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>AWeber has all the tools you need to succeed with email marketing. http://6elrmjmsbs335jwbeybarrry.wpengine.netdna-cdn.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/07/how-creating-custom-segments-can-help-reach-audience_featured-and-social-1200x675-1-300x169.jpg 300w, sizes=\"(max-width: 1200px) 100vw, 1200px\" /></p><!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Delivering the right content to the right people at the right time doesn't have to be complicated. In fact, custom segmentation is a lot easier than it sounds.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>As your audience gets to know you and your content over time, you will learn what interests them by their behavior.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Let’s say you’re a cookbook author. One subscriber may favor vegan recipes, while another may favor recipes with meat. Maybe someone consistently shows interest in a product you sell.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>If you know this about your subscriber base, then you can create custom segments and deliver information you know will delight them.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Custom segmentation lets you break down your audience into groups of people who show interest in specific topics or products — like vegan or meat-based recipes — as well as when they take specific behavioral actions.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>The more you <a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/new-features/its-easier-than-ever-before-to-send-super-personalized-content-to-your-subscribers-using-aweber.htm\">personalize your emails</a>, the more your audience is likely to engage with your content.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>How to use tags to segment your email list&#160;</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><a href=\"https://blog.aweber.com/email-marketing/23-ways-to-tag-and-segment-your-subscribers-in-aweber.htm\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Tags help you organize your subscribers</a> according to interest or behavior. Using tags is an easy way to send content just to audience members that are interested in a particular product or offering.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>The video below shows you how to tag subscribers with a keyword or phrase that identifies their interest or action.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:core-embed/wordpress {\"url\":\"https://aweber.wistia.com/medias/8oeobwr2q3\",\"type\":\"wp-embed\",\"providerNameSlug\":\"wistia-inc\",\"className\":\"\"} -->\n<figure class=\"wp-block-embed-wordpress wp-block-embed is-type-wp-embed is-provider-wistia-inc\"><div class=\"wp-block-embed__wrapper\">\nhttps://aweber.wistia.com/medias/8oeobwr2q3\n</div></figure>\n<!-- /wp:core-embed/wordpress -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>You can also set up the tags ahead of time to automatically be added to your subscribers when they take a specific action.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Tagging is a powerfully-simple way to transform your email marketing. By applying tags, you will make sure your subscribers only receive content relevant to them.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Create a custom segment to send highly-targeted messages</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Creating custom segments lets you send messages to groups of subscribers with a particular tag.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Let's say you are a cookbook author about to launch a new book on vegan cooking.&#160; You know that a vegan cookbook may not appeal to your entire list. If you create a custom segment for users who have expressed interest in vegan recipes or cookbooks, that segment will be most receptive to your message about your vegan cookbook.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:image -->\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image\"><img src=\"https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/x9iSCPE1HE_8T1uU3YZCBbL5VhKoyeolUXthQwQ9gReuRnrK-nDnhIm9Crjr20hHRrYArSE2IGI0tOzfKczY0waRPKxd9-XfIzFXvPLZKffuzwXWbjPIvOI_L9U8K6WoOjM2TLDY\" alt=\"Diagram showing a custom segment for Vegan Tag and Engaged customer.\"/></figure>\n<!-- /wp:image -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>If you have another cookbook for meat lovers, that is an entirely different audience than your vegan audience. You would create a custom segment using tags for people who have actively opened and have a Meat Eater tag.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:image -->\n<figure class=\"wp-block-image\"><img src=\"https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/S5CQhPLod85BNzprLTHHmr5QFYlCx6IoRStibiOYmF56PLPYD3Uq42U_O_apU-j4JbWGAHgSD1JXZYwu_imoeGiPfSoYoPCwWBdH4o4rVt4lfyM3hbuaGRopLZ7Vzfqozx7jKma7\" alt=\"Diagram showing a custom segment for Meat Eater Tag and Engaged customer.\"/></figure>\n<!-- /wp:image -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Once you tag your audience, it is super easy to add a personal touch in your email, thanking them for joining, donations, or purchases. The tag also can serve as a reminder of how they connected with you so you can follow up with them in the future.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:core-embed/wordpress {\"url\":\"https://aweber.wistia.com/medias/8oeobwr2q3\",\"type\":\"wp-embed\",\"providerNameSlug\":\"wistia-inc\",\"className\":\"\"} -->\n<figure class=\"wp-block-embed-wordpress wp-block-embed is-type-wp-embed is-provider-wistia-inc\"><div class=\"wp-block-embed__wrapper\">\nhttps://aweber.wistia.com/medias/8oeobwr2q3\n</div></figure>\n<!-- /wp:core-embed/wordpress -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Save time with dynamic segments</h2>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Rather than manually setting search criteria every time you send an email to a particular audience, create a segment and use it whenever you want to reach that specific audience.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Custom segmentation can also help you improve your open rates, click-through rates, and increase sales or conversions. It can even lead to fewer spam complaints and improve your deliverability.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Why? Because subscribers love content that feels personalized to them. In fact, marketers see an <a href=\"https://monetate.com/blog/the-tipping-point-for-personalized-website-experiences/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">average increase of 20% in sales when using personalized experiences</a>, according to Monetate.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p><strong>Take action! </strong>In the video below, learn how to easily create a segment of subscribers using tags, how to save your dynamic segments, and then send a personalized email within AWeber.&#160;</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:core-embed/youtube {\"url\":\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=w-vArblESXE\",\"type\":\"video\",\"providerNameSlug\":\"youtube\",\"className\":\"wp-embed-aspect-16-9 wp-has-aspect-ratio\"} -->\n<figure class=\"wp-block-embed-youtube wp-block-embed is-type-video is-provider-youtube wp-embed-aspect-16-9 wp-has-aspect-ratio\"><div class=\"wp-block-embed__wrapper\">\nhttps://www.youtube.com/watch?v=w-vArblESXE\n</div></figure>\n<!-- /wp:core-embed/youtube -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading -->\n<h2>Need inspiration? The tag will then automate campaigns to send them relevant product information or content.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:core-embed/wordpress {\"url\":\"https://aweber.wistia.com/medias/a4gevc8agf\",\"type\":\"wp-embed\",\"providerNameSlug\":\"wistia-inc\",\"className\":\"\"} -->\n<figure class=\"wp-block-embed-wordpress wp-block-embed is-type-wp-embed is-provider-wistia-inc\"><div class=\"wp-block-embed__wrapper\">\nhttps://aweber.wistia.com/medias/a4gevc8agf\n</div></figure>\n<!-- /wp:core-embed/wordpress -->\n\n<!-- wp:list {\"ordered\":true} -->\n<ol><li>Go to the element that you want to automate (landing page, sign up form, web page.)</li><li>Enter the tag you want assigned when someone visits that element.</li><li>For prior visitors, you can add the tag manually or through a <a href=\"https://help.aweber.com/hc/en-us/articles/360040500154-How-do-I-update-subscriber-information-through-an-import-\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">bulk import</a>.</li><li>Go to the campaign you want to automate.</li><li>Click \"Replace Trigger\" and enter the tag you want applied. </li><li>Enter the tag.</li><li>Click save and exit.</li></ol>\n<!-- /wp:list -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3} -->\n<h3>Selling your products online</h3>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Assign subscribers a tag based on their purchase or an abandoned cart. Automated campaigns can easily be set up to send relevant content that your audience will find engaging when a tag is applied. Or, start personalizing with one of AWeber’s pre-built campaigns.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:core-embed/wordpress {\"url\":\"https://aweber.wistia.com/medias/ewk6srif5d\",\"type\":\"wp-embed\",\"providerNameSlug\":\"wistia-inc\",\"className\":\"\"} -->\n<figure class=\"wp-block-embed-wordpress wp-block-embed is-type-wp-embed is-provider-wistia-inc\"><div class=\"wp-block-embed__wrapper\">\nhttps://aweber.wistia.com/medias/ewk6srif5d\n</div></figure>\n<!-- /wp:core-embed/wordpress -->\n\n<!-- wp:list {\"ordered\":true} -->\n<ol><li>Click the  integration tab on AWeber's navigation bar.</li><li>If you have the Shopify integration, go to the Cart Abandonment section, select Advanced Features and enter the product, list and tags you want to add.  Then click the green \"Add Automations\" button.                         <strong>Note: </strong>Each ecommerce integration has slightly different options for this step. Visit <a href=\"https://help.aweber.com/hc/en-us/categories/200216396-Knowledge-Base\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">AWeber Knowledge Base</a> for other ecommerce integrations. </li><li>Go to AWeber's <a href=\"https://www.aweber.com/campaign-marketplace.htm\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noreferrer noopener\">Campaign Marketplace</a> to copy the share code for the pre-built ecommerce campaign.</li><li>Go to Campaigns and click the green \"Create a Campaign \" button and select the \"Import a Campaign\" option.</li><li>Enter the code you copied from AWeber's Campaign Marketplace and click the blue \"Import\" button.</li><li>Name your campaign and click the green \"Create\" button.</li><li>Click on the campaign to customize the email and add or update any tags.</li><li>Then activate your campaign.</li></ol>\n<!-- /wp:list -->\n\n<!-- wp:heading {\"level\":3} -->\n<h3>Non-profits and fund-raising</h3>\n<!-- /wp:heading -->\n\n<!-- wp:paragraph -->\n<p>Keep your subscriber list current by adding tags when a new or existing subscriber donates. The tag allows you to add a personal touch in your email, thanking them for their recent donation and serve as a reminder when you need to reach out to them for a donation the following year.</p>\n<!-- /wp:paragraph -->\n\n<!-- wp:core-embed/wordpress {\"url\":\"https://aweber.wistia.com/medias/ir4s93he4y\",\"type\":\"wp-embed\",\"providerNameSlug\":\"wistia-inc\",\"className\":\"\"}
